If one may believe an old tradition , but one which is unsupported by any authentic document , was descended by an illegitimate line from , King of .
His father , da Gama , grand alcalde of and of , in the kingdom of , and commander of , occupied a high position at the court of .
He enjoyed great reputation as a sailor , so much so , that just at the moment when his own unexpected death occurred , King was thinking of giving Gama the command of the fleet which he was desirous of sending to the .
By his marriage with , daughter of de , proveditore of the fortifications of , he had several children , and amongst them , who first reached by doubling the Cape of , and , who accompanied him in that memorable expedition .
It is known that was born at , but the date of his birth is uncertain ; the year 1469 is that generally given , but besides the fact that if this be the correct date , would have been very young -- not more than eight and twenty -- when the important command of the expedition to the was confided to him , there was discovered twenty years ago , amongst the archives , a safe-conduct to granted in 1478 to two persons , da Gama and .
It is scarcely probable that such a passport would have been given to a child of nine years of age , so that this discovery would appear to carry back the birth of the celebrated voyager to an earlier date .
It seems that from an early period of his life , da Gama was destined to follow the career of a sailor , in which his father had distinguished himself .
The first historian of the , de , delights in recalling the fact that he had signalized himself upon the seas .
At one time he was ordered to seize all the ships lying in the ports , in revenge for the capture by pirates during a time of peace of a rich galleon returning from .
Such a mission would only have been confided to an active , energetic and well-tried captain , a clear proof that 's valour and cleverness were highly appreciated by the king .
About this time he married de , one of the highest ladies about the court , and by her he had several children , amongst others da Gama , who became governor of the , and , who , says , by his struggle with in , and by his romantic death , deserves to be reckoned amongst the famous adventurers of the sixteenth century .
All doubt as to the precise date of 's first voyage is now at an end , thanks to the document in the public library at , a paper with which must have been acquainted , and of which M. Ferdinand has published a translation in the and of M. E. Charton .
The date may be fixed with certainty for Saturday , the 8th of July , 1497 .
This expedition had been long ago determined upon , and all its details were minutely arranged .
It was to be composed of four vessels of medium size , `` in order , '' says , `` that they may enter everywhere and again issue forth rapidly . ''
They were solidly constructed , and provided with a triple supply of sails and hawsers ; all the barrels destined to contain water , oil , or wine had been strengthened with iron hoops ; large provisions of all kinds had been made , such as flour , wine , vegetables , drugs , and artillery ; the personnel of the expedition consisted of the best sailors , the cleverest pilots , and the most experienced captains .
, who had received the title of mõr_ , hoisted his flag upon the _Sam-Gabriel_ of 120 tons .
His brother da was on board the _Sam-Raphael_ of 100 tons .
A caravel of 50 tons , the , so named in memory of the pilot , who had sold her to , was commanded by an experienced sailor , , while was the captain of a large barque , laden with provisions and merchandise , destined for exchange with the natives of the countries which should be visited .
de , who had been pilot to , was to regulate the course of the vessels .
The crews , including ten criminals who were put on board to be employed on any dangerous service , amounted to one hundred and sixty persons .
What feeble means these , what almost absurd resources , compared with the grandeur of the mission which these men were to accomplish !
On the 8th of July , at sunrise , advanced towards the vessels , followed by his officers through an immense crowd of people .
Around him were a number of monks and religious persons , who chanted sacred hymns , and besought 's protection for the voyagers .
This departure from must have been a singularly moving scene ; all , whether actors or spectators , mingling their chants , their cries , their adieux and their tears , while the sails , filled by a favourable breeze , bore away Gama and the fortune of towards the open sea .
A large caravel and a smaller barque , which were bound for under the command of , sailed in company with 's fleet .
On the following Saturday , the ships were in sight of the , and passed the night windward of .
When they arrived parallel with the de , a thick fog separated da Gama , , and from the rest of the fleet , but they joined again near the de , which were soon reached .
At fresh stores of meat , water , and wood were taken on board , and the ships were again put into good sailing order .
They quitted the shore of on the 3rd of August .
The voyage was accomplished without any remarkable incidents , and on the 4th of November , anchors were dropped upon the in a bay which received the name of _Santa-Ellena_ .
Eight days were spent there in shipping wood , and in putting everything in order on board the vessels .
It was there that they saw for the first time the , a miserable and degraded race of people who fed upon the flesh of sea-wolves and whales , as well as upon roots .
The carried off some of these natives , and treated them with kindness .
The savages knew nothing of the value of the merchandize which was offered to them , they saw the objects for the first time and were ignorant of their use .
was the only thing which they appeared to prize , wearing in their ears small chains of that metal .
They understood well the use of the zagayes -- a kind of javelin , of which the point is hardened in the fire -- of which three or four of the sailors and even Gama himself had unpleasant experience , while endeavouring to rescue from their hands a certain Velloso , a man who had imprudently ventured into the interior of the country .
This incident has furnished Camoens with one of the most charming episodes of the `` Lusiad . ''
On leaving Santa-Ellena , de , formerly pilot to , declared his belief that they were then ninety miles from the , but in the uncertainty the fleet stood off to sea ; on the 18th of November the Cape of was seen , and the next day it was doubled by the fleet sailing before the wind .
On the 25th the vessels were moored in the of Sam-Braz , where they remained thirteen days , during which time the boat which carried the stores was demolished , and her cargo divided amongst the three other vessels .
During their stay the gave the Bushmen some hawks ' bells and other objects , which , to their surprise , were accepted , for in the time of Diaz the negroes had shown themselves timid and even hostile , and had thrown stones to prevent the crews from procuring water .
Now they brought oxen and sheep , and to show their pleasure at the visit of the , `` they began , '' says , `` to play upon four or five flutes , some set high , some low , a wonderful harmony for negroes , from whom one scarcely looks for music .
They danced also , as dance the blacks , and the mõr commanded the trumpets to sound , and we in our boats danced too , the mõr himself dancing , as soon as he had returned amongst us . ''
What shall we say to this little fête and this mutual serenade between the and the negroes ?
Would any one have expected to behold , a grave man , as his portraits represent him , initiating the negroes into the charms of the pavane .
Unhappily these favourable dispositions were transient , and it was found necessary to have recourse to some hostile demonstrations by means of repeated discharges of artillery .
In this Bay of Sam-Braz Gama erected a padrao , which was thrown down as soon as he was gone .
The fleet soon passed the , the furthest point reached by .
Here the ships experienced the effects of a strong current , but of which the violence was neutralized thanks to a favourable wind .
On the 25th of December , Day , the country of was discovered .
The ships had sustained some damage , and fresh water was needed ; it was therefore urgent for them to find some harbour , which they succeeded in doing on the 10th of January , 1498 .
The blacks whom the saw here upon landing were people of greater stature than those whom they had hitherto met with .
Their arms were a large bow with long arrows , and a zagaye tipped with iron .
They were , a race very superior to the .
Such happy relations were quickly established with them that gave the country the name of the of People ( da bon Gente_ ) .

A little further on , while still sailing up the coast , two Mussulman traders , one wearing a turban , the other a hood of green satin , came to visit the , with a young man who , `` from what could be understood from their signs , belonged to a very distant country , and who said he had already seen ships as large as ours . ''
da Gama , took this as a proof that he was now approaching those lands , which had been so long and so eagerly sought .
For this reason he named the river which flowed into the sea at this place dos ( River of good tokens ) .
Unhappily the first symptoms of scurvy appeared at this time amongst the crews , and soon there were many sailors upon the sick list .
On the 10th of March the expedition cast anchor before the of , where , as learnt through his interpreters , there were several merchants of extraction , who carried on trade with .
and silver , cloth and spices , pearls and rubies , formed the staple of their commerce .
Gama at the same time was assured that in pursuing the line of the coast , he would find numerous cities ; `` Whereat we were so joyful , '' says in his naïve and valuable narrative , `` that we wept for pleasure , praying God to grant us health that we might see all that which we had so much desired . ''
The , who imagined he was dealing with , came on board several times and was magnificently entertained ; he returned the civility by sending presents , and even furnished Gama with two skilful pilots , but when some merchants who had traded in told him that these foreigners , far from being , were in reality the worst enemies of the Mahometans , the viceroy , disgusted at his mistake , made preparations for seizing the by treachery , and killing them .
was obliged to point his artillery at the town and threaten to reduce it to ashes before he could obtain the water needed for the prosecution of his voyage .
flowed , and da captured two barques , whose rich cargo was divided amongst the sailors .
The ships quitted this inhospitable town , on the 29th of March , and the voyage continued , a close surveillance being kept over the pilots , whom was obliged to cause to be flogged .
On the 4th of April the coast was seen , and on the 8th Mombasa or was reached , a town , according to the pilots , inhabited by and .
The fleet dropped anchor outside the harbour , and did not enter it , notwithstanding the enthusiastic reception given to them .
Already the were reckoning upon meeting at mass the next day with the Christians of the , when during the night , the flag-ship was approached by a _zacra_ , having on board a hundred armed men , who endeavoured to enter the ships in a body , which was refused them .
The king of was informed of all that had occurred at , but pretending ignorance , he sent presents to , proposing to him to establish a factory in his capital , and assuring him that so soon as he should have entered the port , he might take on board a cargo of spices and aromatics .
The mõr , suspecting nothing , immediately sent two men to announce his entry for the morrow ; already they were weighing anchor when the flag-ship refusing to tack , the anchor was let fall again .
In graceful and poetic fiction , affirms that it was the led by , the protectress of the , who stayed their ships when on the point of entering the port .
At this moment all the Moors on board the fleet quitted it simultaneously , whilst the pilots threw themselves into the sea .
Two Moors who were put to the question with a drop of hot oil , confessed that the intention was to take all the prisoners as soon as they should be inside the harbour .
During the night the endeavoured several times to climb on board and to cut the cables in order to run the ships aground , but each time they were discovered .
Under these circumstances no prolonged stay was possible at , but it had been long enough for all those ill of scurvy to recover their health .
At the distance of four-and-twenty miles from land , the fleet captured a barque richly laden with gold , silver , and provisions .
The next day arrived at , a rich and flourishing city , whose gilded minarets , sparkling in the sunshine , and whose mosques of dazzling whiteness , stood out against a sky of the most intense blue .
The reception of the at was at first very cold , the capture of the barque the evening before being already known there , but as soon as explanations had been given , the people became cordial .
The king 's son came to visit the admiral , accompanied by a train of courtiers splendidly dressed , and a choir of musicians , who played upon various instruments .
The greatest astonishment was shown at the artillery practice , for the invention of gunpowder was not yet known on the east coast of .
A solemn treaty was made , ratified by oaths upon the and the , and cemented by an interchange of presents .
From this moment the ill-will , the treachery , the difficulties of all kinds which had hitherto beset the expedition , ceased as if by magic : this must be attributed to the generosity of the King of , and to the aid which he furnished to the .
to the promise which he had made to da Gama , the king sent him a Gujerat pilot named , a man well instructed in navigation , understanding the use of charts , of the compass and the quadrant , and who rendered the most important service to the expedition .
After a stay of nine days the fleet weighed anchor for .
The coasting plan hitherto pursued was now to be abandoned , and the time was come when , in reliance upon the blessing of , the must venture out upon the wide ocean , without other guide than an unknown pilot furnished by a king whose kind welcome had not sufficed to lull to sleep the suspicions of the foreigners .
And yet , thanks to the ability and loyalty of this pilot , thanks also to the clemency of the sea , and to the wind being constantly in its favour , the fleet , after a twenty-three days ' voyage , reached the land on the 17th May , and the next day anchored at the distance of six miles below .
The enthusiasm on board was great .
At last they had arrived in those rich and wonderful countries .
, dangers , sickness , all were forgotten .
The object of their long labours was attained !
Or rather , it seemed to be so , for there was still needed the possession of the treasures and rich productions of .
Scarcely were the anchors dropped when four boats came off from the shore , performing evolutions around the fleet , and apparently inviting the sailors to disembark .
But , rendered cautious by the occurrences at and , sent on shore one of the criminals who were on board , to act as a scout ; ordering him to walk through the town and endeavour to ascertain the temper of its inhabitants .
Surrounded by an inquisitive crowd , assailed by questions to which he could not reply , this man was conducted to the house of a Moor named , who spoke , and to whom he gave a short account of the voyage of the fleet .
returned with him on board , and his first words on setting foot on the ship were `` Good luck !
quantities of rubies , quantities of emeralds ! ''
, was at once engaged as interpreter .
The King of was at this time at a distance of forty-five miles from his capital , so the mõr despatched two men to announce the arrival of an ambassador from the King of , being the bearer of letters to him from his sovereign .
The king at once sent a pilot , with orders to take the ships into the safer roadstead of , and promised to return himself on the morrow to ; this he did , and ordered his or to invite Gama to land and open negotiations .
In spite of the supplications of his brother , da Gama , who represented to him the dangers which he might incur , and those to which his death would expose the expedition , the mõr set out for the shore , upon which an enormous crowd of people were awaiting him .
The idea that they were in the midst of a population was so rooted in the minds of all the members of the expedition , that , on passing by a pagoda on the way , entered it to perform his devotions .
One of his companions , however , de Saa , noticing the hideous pictures upon the walls , was less credulous , and whilst throwing himself upon his knees , said aloud , `` If that be a devil , I intend nevertheless to adore only the true God ! ''
A mental reservation which caused amusement to the admiral .
Near the gates of the town the crowd was even more closely packed .
and his companions , under the guidance of the , had some difficulty in reaching the palace , where the king , who in the narrative is called the `` , '' was awaiting them with extreme impatience .
Ushered into halls splendidly decorated with silken stuffs and carpets , and in which burned the most exquisite perfumes , the found themselves in the presence of the .
He was magnificently attired , and loaded with jewels , the pearls and diamonds which he wore being of extraordinary size .
The king ordered refreshments to be served to the strangers , and permitted them to be seated , a peculiar mark of favour in a country where the sovereign is usually only addressed with the most lowly prostrations .
The afterwards passed into another apartment , to hear with his own ears , as was proudly demanded by , the reasons for the embassy and the desire felt by the King of to conclude a treaty of commerce and alliance with the King of .
The listened to 's discourse , and replied that he should be happy to consider himself the friend and brother of King Emmanuel , and that he would , by the aid of , send ambassadors to .
[ Illustration : 's interview with the .
There are certain proverbs of which the force is not affected by change of latitude , and the truth of that one which says , `` The days succeed each other and have no similarity , '' was proved the next day at .
The enthusiasm which had been aroused in the mind of the by the ingenious discourse of , and the hope it had awakened of the establishment of a profitable trade with , vanished at the sight of the presents which were to be given him .
`` Twelve pieces of striped cloth , twelve cloaks with scarlet hoods , six hats , and four branches of coral , accompanied by a box containing six large basons , a chest of sugar , and four kegs , two filled with oil , and two with honey , '' certainly did not constitute a very magnificent offering .
At sight of it , the prime minister laughed , declaring that the poorest merchant from brought richer presents , and that the king would never accept of such ridiculous trifles .
After this affront Gama again visited the , but it was only after long waiting in the midst of a mocking crowd , that he was admitted to the presence of the king .
The latter reproached him in a contemptuous manner for having nothing to offer him , while pretending to be the subject of a rich and powerful king .
replied with boldness , and produced the letters of , which were couched in flattering terms , and contained a formal promise to send merchandise to .
The , pleased at this prospect , then inquired with interest about the productions and resources of , and gave permission to to disembark and sell his goods .
But this abrupt change in the humour of the was not at all agreeable to the and traders , whose dealings made the prosperity of .
They could not look on quietly whilst foreigners were endeavouring for their own advantage to turn aside the commerce which had been hitherto entirely in their hands ; they resolved , therefore , to leave no stone unturned to drive away once for all these formidable rivals from the shores of .
Their first care was to gain the ear of the ; then they painted in the blackest colours these insatiable adventurers , these bold robbers , whose only object was to spy out the strength and resources of the town , that they might return in force to pillage it , and to massacre those who should venture to oppose their designs .
Upon arriving at the roadstead of , found no boat to take him off to the ships , and was forced to sleep on shore .
The never left him , continually seeking to prove to him the necessity of bringing the ships nearer to the land ; and when the admiral positively refused to consent to this , he declared him to be his prisoner .
He had very little idea as yet of the firmness of 's character .
Some armed boats were sent to surprise the ships , but the , having received secret intelligence from the admiral of all that had happened , were on their guard , and their enemies dared not use open force .
, still a prisoner , threatened the with the anger of the , whom he imagined could never thus have violated the duties of hospitality , but seeing that his menaces produced no effect , he tried bribery , presenting the minister with several pieces of stuff , who , thereupon at once altered his demeanour .
`` If the , '' said he , `` had but kept the promise they had made to the king , of disembarking their merchandise , the admiral would long ago have returned on board his ships . ''
Gama at once sent an order to bring the goods to land , opened a shop for their sale , of which the superintendence was given to , brother to the discoverer of the Cape of , and was then allowed to go back to his ships .
The placed obstacles in the way of the sale of the merchandise by depreciating its value ; sent his agent to the to complain of the perfidy of the and of the bad treatment to which he had been subjected , requesting at the same time permission to move his place of sale to , where he hoped that the goods would be more easily disposed of .
This request was favourably received , and friendly relations were maintained , in spite of the intrigues , until the 10th of , 1498 .
On that day went to announce 's impending departure to the king , reminding him of his promise to send an embassy to , and asking him to allow Gama a specimen of each of the productions of the country .
These were to be paid for on the first sale of goods which should take place after the departure of the fleet , it being intended that the employés of the factory should remain at during 's absence .
The , instigated by the traders , not only refused to execute his promise , but demanded the payment of 600 _seraphins_ as customs ' duty , ordering at the same time the seizure of the merchandise , and making prisoners of the men employed in the factory .
Such an outrage , such contempt for the rights of nations , called for prompt vengeance , but understood the art of dissimulation ; however , on receiving a visit on board from some rich merchants , he detained them , and sent to the to demand an exchange of prisoners .
The king 's reply not being sent within the time specified by the admiral , the latter set sail and anchored at the distance of sixteen miles from .
After another fruitless attack by the , the two agents returned on board , and a portion of the hostages whom had secured were given up .
brought back with him a curious letter from the to the King of .
It was written upon a palm leaf , and shall be quoted in all its strange laconicism , so different from the usual grandiloquence of the oriental style : -- `` Vasco da Gama , a noble of thy palace , is come into my country which I have permitted .
In my kingdom there is much cinnamon , cloves , and pepper , with many precious stones , and what I desire from thy country is gold , silver , coral , and scarlet .
On the morrow , Mouçaïda the of Tunis who had served as interpreter to the , and had been a great assistance to them in their negotiations with the , came to seek an asylum on board the ships .
The merchandise had not been brought back on the appointed day , and the mõr now resolved to carry away with him the men whom he had kept as hostages , but the fleet was becalmed at several miles distance from , and was attacked by twenty armed boats , which were with difficulty kept at a distance by the artillery , until they were forced by a violent storm to take shelter under the coast .
The admiral was sailing along the coast of the , and had permitted some of the sailors to go on shore to gather fruit and collect cinnamon bark , when he perceived eight boats , which appeared to be coming towards him .
recalled the men , and sailed forward to meet the , who made the greatest haste to flee from him , but not without leaving a boat laden with cocoa , and provisions , in the hands of the .
On arriving at the , had the recalked , and his own ship drawn up on shore for repairs .
The sailors were busy over this work when they were again attacked , but without more success than heretofore .
The next day witnessed the arrival of an individual forty years of age , dressed in style , who began to speak to the in excellent , telling them that he was a native of , and had been torn from his country while still young , that he was a , but without the possibility of practising his religion .
He was in a high position at the court of the king of the country , who had sent him to them , to place at their disposal all that the country contained which could minister to their comfort .
These offers of service , so different from the welcome accorded to them hitherto , excited the suspicions of the , and they were not long in discovering that this adventurer was in command of the boats which had attacked them the day before .
Upon this they had him scourged until he confessed that he had come to discover whether it were possible to attack the fleet with advantage , and he ended by affirming that all the inhabitants of the sea-shore were in league to destroy the .
He was retained on board , the work upon the ships was hurried forward , and as soon as water and provisions had been taken in , sail was made for a return to .
In consequence of dead calms and contrary winds , the expedition was three months , all but three days , in reaching the coast .
During this long voyage the crews suffered terribly from scurvy , and thirty sailors perished .
In each ship , only seven or eight men were in a condition to work the vessel , and very often the officers themselves were forced to lend a hand .
`` Whence I can affirm , '' says , `` that if the time in which we sailed across those seas had been prolonged a fortnight , nobody from hence would have navigated them after us ... . And the captains having held a council upon the matter , it was resolved that in case of similar winds catching us again , to return towards , there to take refuge . ''
On the 2nd of February , 1499 , the found themselves at last abreast of a great town on the coast of , called , distant 300 miles from .

A few days afterwards the rich and salubrious plains of came in sight , and here they cast anchor .
The king hastened to send off fresh provisions and oranges for the invalids on board .
The reception given by him to the was in every particular most affectionate , and the friendship which had arisen during 's first visit to was greatly strengthened .
The of sent for the King of a horn made of ivory and a number of other presents , entreating Gama at the same time to receive a young on board his ship , that through him the king might learn how earnestly he desired his friendship .
The five days ' rest at was of the greatest benefit to the , at its expiration they again set sail .
Soon after passing Mombaz they were obliged to burn the _Sam-Raphael_ , the crews being too much reduced to be able to work three ships .
They discovered the of , anchored in the of Sam-Braz , and on the 20th February , a favourable wind enabled them to double the Cape of , when they again found themselves upon the .
The breeze remaining favourable , helped forward the return of the mariners , and at the end of twenty-seven days , they had arrived in the neighbourhood of the of .
On the 25th of April , captain of the , eager to be the first to carry to Emmanuel the news of the discovery of the , separated himself from his chief , and without touching , as had been arranged , at the de , made sail direct for , arriving there on the 10th of July .
During this time the unfortunate Gama was plunged in the most profound sorrow , for his brother , da Gama , who had shared his fatigues and sufferings , and who was to be a partaker of his glory , seemed to be slowly dying .
At , da Gama , now returned to well known and much frequented seas , gave up the command of his ships to da , and chartered a fast-sailing caravel , to hasten as much as possible his beloved invalid 's return to his native country .
But all hope was vain , and the caravel only arrived at in time to inter there the body of the brave and sympathizing da Gama .
Upon his arrival in , which must have taken place during the early part of September , the admiral was received with stately festivals .
Of the 160 whom he had taken with him , fifty-five only returned with him .
The loss was great certainly , but what was it compared with the great advantages to be hoped for ?
The public realized this , and gave the most enthusiastic reception to .
The King , , added to his own titles that of of the conquests and of the navigation of , , , and the ; but he allowed two years to pass before rewarding Gama .
He then bestowed upon him the title of of the , and authorized him to use the prefix of before his name , a privilege then rarely granted .
Also , doubtless to make da Gama forget the tardiness with which his services had been rewarded , the king gave him 1000 crowns , a considerable sum for that period , and also conceded to him certain privileges in connexion with the commerce of the , which were likely speedily to make his fortune .

On the 9th of March , 1500 , a fleet of thirteen vessels left , under the command of ; on board , as a volunteer , was de , who in his poem the `` , '' was to render illustrious the valour and adventurous spirit of his countrymen .
But little is known of , and nothing of the reason which had gained him the command of this important expedition .
belonged to one of the most illustrious families in , and his father , , lord of da , was mõr of .
had married de , first lady in waiting to the , daughter of .
If it be asked whether had made himself famous by some important maritime discovery , we answer there is no reason to think so , for in that case the historians would have recorded it .
But it is difficult to believe that he owed to court favour alone the command of an expedition in which such men as , the companion of , and de sailed under his orders .
Why had not this mission been confided to , who had been at home for six months , and whose knowledge of the countries to be visited and of the manners of their inhabitants , seemed to point him out as the fittest man for the service ?
Had he not yet recovered from the fatigues of his first voyage ?
Or had his grief for the loss of a brother who had died almost within sight of the coasts of so deeply affected him , that he desired to remain in retirement ?
May it not rather have been that King was jealous of the fame of , and did not wish to give him the opportunity of increasing his renown ?
These are problems which perhaps history may be for ever unable to solve .
It is easy to believe in the realization of those things which we ardently desire .
imagined that the of would not object to the establishment of shops and factories in his country , and , the bearer of presents of such magnificence as to obliterate the memory of the shabbiness of those offered by , received orders to obtain from the an interdict , forbidding any Moor to carry on trade in his capital .
The new Capitam mõr was in the first place to visit , to offer rich presents to its king , and to restore to him the Moor who had come to with .
Sixteen friars were sent out on board the fleet , charged to carry the knowledge of the to the distant countries of .
The fleet had sailed for thirteen days and had passed the de , when it was discovered that one of the ships , under the command of d'Ataïde , was no longer in company .
The rest of the ships lay to for some time to await her , but in vain , and the twelve vessels then continued their navigation upon the open sea , and not , as had been the manner hitherto , steering simply from cape to cape along the shores of .

Perhaps even the mõr , who must , in common with the rest of his countrymen , have been acquainted with the discoveries of , may have had the secret hope , by keeping to the west , of arriving at some region unvisited by the great navigator .
The fact remains , whether it is to be accounted for by a storm or by some secret design , that the fleet was out of the right way for doubling the Cape of when , on the 22nd of April , a high mountain was seen , and soon afterwards a long stretch of coast , which received the name of , changed afterwards to that of .
This was , and the point where now stands .
On the 28th , after a skilful reconnaissance of the coasts had been made by , the sailors landed upon the shores , and became aware of a delicious mildness of temperature , with a luxuriance of vegetation greatly exceeding anything which they had seen on the coasts of or of .
The natives formed themselves in groups around the sailors , without showing the least sign of fear .
They were almost naked , and bore upon the wrist a tame parroquet , after the fashion in which the gentlemen of carry their hawks or their gerfalcons .
On Sunday , the 26th of April , a solemn mass was celebrated on the shore in sight of the , whose silence and attitude of respect excited the admiration of the .
On the 1st of May a large cross and a padrao were erected on the shore , and formally took possession of the country in the name of the King of .
His first care after this formality was accomplished was to despatch de to , to announce the discovery of this rich and fertile country .
took with him the narrative of the expedition written by de , and an important astronomical document , the work of , in which was doubtless stated the exact situation of the new conquest .
Before setting out for , put on land two criminals , whom he ordered to ascertain the resources and riches of the country , as well as the manners and customs of the inhabitants .
These wise and far-sighted measures speak much for 's prudence and sagacity .
[ Illustration : Cabral takes formal possession of . ]
It was the 2nd of May when the fleet lost sight of .
All on board , rejoicing over this happy commencement of the voyage , believed in the prospect of an easy and rapid success , when the appearance of a brilliant comet on eight consecutive days struck the ignorant and simple minds of the sailors with terror ; they considered it must be a bad omen , and for this once events appeared to justify superstition .
A fearful storm arose , waves mountains high broke over the ships , whilst the wind blew furiously and rain fell without ceasing .
When the sun at length succeeded in piercing the thick curtain of clouds which almost entirely intercepted his rays , a horrible scene was disclosed .
The water looked thick and black , large patches of a livid white colour flecked the foaming , crested waves , while during the night phosphorescent lights , streaking the immense plain of water , marked out the course of the ships with a train of fire .
For two-and-twenty days , without truce or mercy , the ships were battered by the furious elements .
The terrified sailors were utterly prostrate ; they vainly exhausted their prayers and vows , and obeyed the orders of their officers only from the force of habit ; from the first day they had given up any hope of their lives being spared , and only awaited the moment when they should all be submerged .
When light at length returned and the billows became calm , each crew , thinking themselves to be perhaps the sole survivors , looked eagerly over the sea in search of their companions .
Three ships met together again with a joy which the sad reality soon abated .
Eight vessels were missing ; four had been engulfed by a gigantic water-spout during the last days of the storm .
One of these had been commanded by , the discoverer of the Cape of : he had been drowned by these murderous waves , the defenders , according to , of the empire of the east against the nations of the west , who had for so many centuries coveted her marvellous riches .
During this long series of storms the had been doubled and the fleet was approaching the coast of .
On the 20th of July was signalled .
The Moors of this place showed a more agreeable disposition than they had done when was there , and furnished the with two pilots , who conducted them to , an island famed for the trade in gold-dust which was carried on with .
There Cabral found two of the missing ships , which had been driven to this island by the wind .
A plot was on foot in for a wholesale massacre of the , but this was frustrated by a prompt departure from the island , and the ships arrived at without any untoward incident .
The stay of the fleet in this port was the occasion of fêtes and rejoicings without number , and soon , revictualled , repaired , and furnished with excellent pilots , the vessels sailed for , where they arrived on the 13th of December , 1500 .
This time , thanks to the power of their arms as well as to the richness of the presents offered to the , the reception was different , and the versatile prince agreed to all the demands of : namely , a monopoly of the trade in aromatics and spicery , and the right of seizure upon all vessels which should infringe this privilege .
For some time the Moors dissembled their resentment , but when they had succeeded in thoroughly exasperating the population against the foreigners , they rushed at a given signal into the factory which was under the direction of , and massacred fifty of the , whom they surprised in it .
for this outrage was not slow ; ten boats moored in the port were taken , pillaged , and burnt before the eyes of the , who were powerless to render opposition ; afterwards the town was bombarded , and was half-buried under its ruins .
When this affair was concluded , , continuing the exploration of the coast , arrived at , where the , a vassal of the , hastened to conclude an alliance with the , eagerly seizing this opportunity to declare himself independent .
Although by this time his fleet was richly laden , made a visit to , where he entered into a treaty with the of the country ; then , being impatient to return home , he set sail for .
While coasting along that shore of , which is washed by the , he discovered , a place which had escaped the observation of .
On the 13th of July , 1501 , arrived at , where he had the joy of finding the two remaining ships which he had imagined to be lost .
It is pleasant to believe that he received the welcome merited by the important results obtained in this memorable expedition .
Although contemporary historians are silent upon the incidents of his life after his return , recent research has been rewarded by the discovery of his tomb at , and M. Ferdinand has happily proved that , like da Gama , he received the title of as a reward for his glorious deeds .
Whilst he was returning to Alvarès Cabral might have encountered a fleet of four caravels under the command of da Nova , which King had despatched to give fresh vigour to the commercial relations which had been charged to establish in the Indies .
This new expedition doubled the Cape of without misadventure , discovered between and an unknown island , which was named after the commander of the fleet , and arrived at , where was informed of the events which had taken place at .
He felt that he had not forces at his disposal sufficient to justify him in going to punish the , and not wishing to endanger the prestige of arms by the risk of a reverse , he steered for and , of which the kings , although tributaries of the , had entered into alliance with .
Da had already taken on board 1000 hundredweights of pepper , 50 of ginger , and 450 of cinnamon , when he received warning that a considerable fleet , coming apparently from , was advancing with hostile intentions .
If he had hitherto been more concerned with trade than with war , he did not the less in these critical circumstances display a bold and courageous spirit worthy of his predecessors .
He accepted the combat , notwithstanding the apparent superiority of the , and partly by the skilful arrangements which he made , partly by the power of his guns , he managed to disperse , to take , or to sink the hostile vessels .
Perhaps Da Nova ought to have profited by the terror which his victory had spread along the coast , and the temporary exhaustion of the resources , to strike a great blow by the taking of .
But we are too far removed in time from the events , and know too little of their details , to appreciate with impartiality the reasons which induced the admiral to return immediately to .
It was during this latter part of his voyage that discovered the small island of in the midst of the .
A curious story attaches to this discovery .
A certain had followed to the ; this man , wishing to marry a , was forced for this purpose to renounce and become a .
Upon 's visit , having had enough either of his wife or of her religion , he begged to be taken back to his country , and returned to his old creed .
Upon arriving at , , in obedience to a sudden idea , which he regarded as an inspiration from on high , requested to be landed there , in order , as he said , to expiate his detestable apostasy and to atone for it by his devotion to humanity .
His will appeared so fixed that was forced to consent , and he left him there , having given him at his request various seeds of fruits and vegetables .
It must be added that this singular hermit worked for four years at the clearing and planting of the island with such success , that ships were soon able to call there to revictual during their long passage from to the Cape of .
The successive expeditious of , , and had conclusively proved that an uninterrupted commerce must not be reckoned upon , nor a continued exchange of merchandise , with the population of the , who , while their own independence and liberty were respected had each time leagued together against the .
That trade with which they so persistently refused , must be forced upon them , and for that purpose permanent military establishments must be formed , capable of overawing the malcontents , and even in case of necessity of taking possession of the country .
But to whom should such an important mission be entrusted ?
The choice could scarcely be doubtful , and da Gama was unanimously chosen to take the command of the powerful armament which was in preparation .
had ten ships under his own immediate command , while his second brother da Gama , and his cousin , had each five ships under his orders , but they were both to recognise da Gama as their chief .
The ceremonies which preceded the departure of the fleet from were of a particularly grave and solemn character .
King , followed by the whole court , repaired to the cathedral in the midst of an enormous crowd , and there called down blessings from heaven upon this expedition , partly religious , partly military , while the blessed the banner which was entrusted to .
The admiral 's first care was to visit and , towns of which he had had reason to complain in the course of his first voyage .
Being anxious to establish harbours for refuge , and revictualling of ships , he established there merchants ' offices , and laid the foundations of forts .
He also levied a heavy tribute upon the of , and then sailed for the coast of .
When had arrived off , he perceived on the 3rd of October a vessel of large tonnage , which appeared to him to be richly laden .
It was the _Merii_ bringing back from a great number of pilgrims belonging to all the countries of .
attacked the ship without provocation , captured her and put to death more than three hundred men who were on board .
children alone were saved and taken to , where they were baptized , and entered the army of .
This frightful massacre , besides being quite in accordance with the ideas of the period , was calculated according to , to strike terror into the mind : it did nothing of the sort .
This hateful and useless cruelty has left a stain of blood upon the hitherto pure fame of the admiral .

As soon as he arrived at , obtained an audience of the , who authorized him to establish a counting-house , and to build a fort .
At the same time a treaty of alliance , offensive and defensive was concluded .
After setting the labourers to work , and installing his agent , the admiral set sail for , where he intended to summon the to a reckoning for his disloyalty , as well as for the murder of the who had been surprised in the factory .
Although the of had been informed of the arrival in the Indies of his formidable enemies , he had taken no military precautions , and thus , when presented himself before the town , he was able to seize some vessels anchored in the port and to make a hundred prisoners , without encountering any resistance ; afterwards he granted the Zamorin a respite of four days , in which to make atonement to the for the murder of , and to refund the value of the merchandise which had been stolen on that occasion .
The time specified had scarcely elapsed when the bodies of fifty of the prisoners were strung up at the yard-arms of the vessels , where they remained exposed to the view of the town during the whole day .
In the evening the feet and hands of these expiatory victims were cut off and taken on shore , with a letter from the admiral , declaring that his vengeance would not be limited to this execution .
Accordingly , under cover of the night , the broadsides of the vessels were brought to bear upon the town , which was bombarded for the space of three days .
It will never be known what was the exact number of the slain , but it must have been considerable .
Without reckoning those killed by the fire of the cannon and the muskets , a great number of were buried beneath the ruins of the buildings , or perished in the conflagration , which destroyed a portion of the town of .
The had been one of the first to take flight , and fortunate was it for him that he had done so , for his palace was amongst the buildings which were demolished .
At length , satisfied with having transformed this heretofore rich and populous city into a heap of ruins , and considering his vengeance satiated , and that the lesson so taught would be profitable , set sail for , leaving behind him Vincent Sodrez , with several ships , to continue the blockade .
, the sovereign of , informed the admiral that he had been eagerly solicited by the to take advantage of the confidence reposed in him by the , to surprise and seize them , in consequence of which intelligence , and to reward the integrity of the king whose loyalty had exposed him to the enmity of the of , , when starting for with a valuable cargo , left with ships sufficient to enable him to await in safety the arrival of another squadron .
During 's return voyage the only noteworthy incident that occurred was the defeat of another fleet .
The admiral arrived in on the 20th of Once more the eminent services rendered by this great man went unrecognised , or rather they were not appreciated as they deserved .
, who had just laid the foundations of the colonial empire of in , remained for one and twenty years without employment , and it was only through the intercession of the of , that he obtained the title of de Vidigueyra .
A too common instance this of ingratitude , but one which it is never _mal à propos_ to stigmatize as it deserves .
Scarcely had set out for , before the at the instigation of the , who saw their commercial supremacy more and more compromised , assembled his allies at with the object of attacking the King of and of punishing him for the counsel and assistance which he had given to the .
The unfortunate 's fidelity was now put to a hard proof .
Besieged in his capital by a large force , he saw himself all at once deprived of the aid of those for whose advantage he had incurred so great a risk .
and several of his captains had deserted the post , where both honour and gratitude required them to remain , and if need were , to die in the discharge of their duty ; they forsook to go and cruise in the neighbourhood of , and at the entrance to the , where they calculated that the annual pilgrimage to was likely to ensure them some rich booty .
The agent vainly represented to them the unworthiness of their conduct , they set out in haste , to escape from these inconvenient reproaches .
The King of , betrayed by some of the ( military nobles ) of his palace , who had been gained over by the , soon saw his capital carried by assault , and was obliged to seek refuge upon an inaccessible rock in the little of , with those Portuguese who had remained faithful to him .
When he was reduced to the last extremity , an emissary was sent to him by the , to promise him pardon and oblivion of his offences if he would give up to him the .
But , whose fidelity can not be sufficiently commended , answered , `` that the might use his rights of victory ; that he was not ignorant of the perils by which he was menaced , but that it was not in the power of any man to make him a traitor and a perjurer . ''
No one could have made a nobler return than this for the desertion and cowardice of .
had arrived at the Straits of Bab-el-Mandeb , when a fearful tempest occurred , in which his ship split upon the rocks , and he and his brother perished .
The survivors regarded this event as a judgment of for their bad conduct , and they made haste , with all sails set to return to .
They were detained by contrary winds at the , and were there joined by another squadron under the command of d'Albuquerque , who had sailed from almost at the same time as his cousin d'Albuquerque the most distinguished captain of the period , who with the title of mõr had started from at the beginning of April , 1503 .
The arrival of d'Albuquerque placed the affairs , which had been so gravely compromised by the criminal conduct of , upon a better footing , and at the same time effected the rescue of , their sole and faithful ally .
The besiegers fled at the sight of the squadron , without even a show of resistance , and the Europeans in conjunction with the troops of the King of ravaged the .
As a consequence of these events , allowed his allies to construct a second fortress in his dominions , and authorised an augmentation of the number and importance of their mercantile houses .
This was the moment that witnessed the arrival of d'Albuquerque , the man destined to be the real creator of the Empire in the Indies .
, , and , had prepared the way , but was the leader of large views who was needed to determine which were the principal towns that must be seized in order to place the dominion upon a solid and lasting basis .
Thus every particular of the history of this man who showed so great a genius for colonisation , is of the deepest interest , and it is well worth while to record some particulars of his family , his education , and his early exploits .
d'Alboquerque or d'Albuquerque , was born in 1453 at , eighteen miles from .
Through his father d'Albuquerque , the of , he was descended , but illegitimately , from King Diniz ; and through his mother from the , the great explorers .
Brought up at the court of , he there received as liberal and thorough an education as was possible at the period .
He made an especial study of the great writers of antiquity , whose influence may be traced in the majesty and accuracy of his own style , and of mathematics of which he knew as much as could be learnt at that time .
After staying for some years at , an town which was under the dominion of , he returned to , and was appointed of the Horse to , a prince whose chief anxiety was to extend the name and power of beyond the seas .
It is evident that it was to the constant attendance upon the king imposed upon him by the duties of his office , that owed the inclination of his mind towards geographical studies , and his anxious desire to find the means of giving to his country the of the .
He had already taken part in an expedition sent to the succour of the King of against an incursion of the , and in 1489 , had been charged with the commission of revictualling and defending the fortress of , upon the coast of .
We must now return from this digression and take up the history of , from the time of his arrival in in 1503 .
It took him but a few days to become thoroughly aware of the position of affairs ; he perceived that the commerce of must depend upon conquest for its power of development .
But his first enterprise was proportioned to the feebleness of his resources ; he laid siege to , which he wished to make a military station for his countrymen , and then with two ships he undertook a reconnaissance of the coast of .
Being attacked quite unexpectedly both by land and sea , he was on the point of yielding when the fortunate arrival of his cousin turned the combat , and put the 's troops to flight .
The importance of this victory was considerable ; the conquerors remained masters of an immense booty and quantities of precious stones , which had the result of stimulating the spirit of covetousness ; at the same time it confirmed in his designs , for the execution of which the consent of the king was needful , and also more considerable resources .
He therefore set out on his return to , where he arrived in , 1504 .
This same year , King Emmanuel wishing to organize a regular government in the , had made da Cunha his viceroy , but having become temporarily blind was obliged to resign his power before he had exercised it .
The king 's choice next fell upon d'Almeida , who set out with his son in 1505 .
It will be soon seen what were the means which he considered should be employed to assure the triumph of his countrymen .
On the 6th of March , 1506 , sixteen vessels left under the command of da , who had by that time regained his health .
With him went , carrying with him , but unknown to himself , his patent of of .
He was ordered not to open the sealed packet until three years should have expired , when would have completed the term of his mission .
This numerous fleet , after having stopped at the de and discovered in , steered directly for the unexplored parts of the , and went so far south that the old chroniclers assert that several sailors being too lightly clad died from cold , while the others were scarcely able to work the ships .
In 37 degrees 8 minutes south latitude , and 14 degrees 21 minutes west longitude , discovered three small uninhabited islands , of which the largest still bears his name .
A storm prevented a landing there , and so completely dispersed the fleet that the admiral could not get his vessels together again before he arrived at .
In sailing along this coast he explored the island of or Sam-Lorenzo , which had just been discovered by , who was in command of eight vessels which was sending back to ; it was not thought advisable to make a settlement upon the island .
After having wintered at , landed three ambassadors at , who were to reach by travelling overland , then he anchored at , which , one of his lieutenants had been unable to subjugate .
The now laid siege to this town , which resisted bravely but which yielded in the end , thanks to the courage of the enemy and the perfection of their arms .
The population was massacred without mercy , and the town pillaged and burnt .
Upon , another town on the , tried but in vain , to impose his authority .
The strength of the town and the stubborn resolution shown by the numerous population as well as the approach of winter forced him to raise the siege .
He then turned his arms against , at the entrance of the Gulf of , where he carried the fortress .
The whole of the garrison were put to the sword , the only man spared being an old blind soldier , who was discovered hidden in a well .
When asked how he had been able to get down there , he answered , -- '' The blind only see the road which leads to liberty . ''
At , the two chiefs constructed the fort of , intended by to command the Gulf of and the , by the of Bab-el-Mandeb , thus cutting one of the lines of communication with the Indies , which was the most used by the Venetians .
Here Da Cunha and separated , the former going to to obtain a cargo of spices , the latter officially invested with the title of mõr , and bent on the realization of his vast schemes , setting out on the 10th of , 1507 , for , having left his nephew Alfonzo da in charge of the new fortress .
He took in succession , and as if to get his hand in for the work , , where were found immense stores , and , which he gave up to pillage , fire , and destruction , in order to avenge a series of acts of treachery easily understood by those who know the duplicity of these eastern people .
The success which he had just gained at , important as it was , did not content .
He dreamed of other and grander projects , of which the execution was , however , much compromised by the jealousy of the captains under his orders , and notably of da Nova , who contemplated abandoning his chief , and whom was obliged to place under arrest on board his own ship .
After having suppressed these beginnings of disobedience and rebellion , the mõr reached , which was taken after a vigorous resistance .
It is a curious fact that had long heard spoken of , but that as yet he was ignorant of its position .
He knew that this town served as an entrepôt for all the merchandise passing from into .
Its riches and power , the number of its inhabitants and the beauty of its monuments were at that time celebrated throughout the , so much so that there was a common saying , `` If the world be a ring , is the precious stone set in it . ''
had resolved to take this town , not only because in itself it was a prize worth having , but also because it commanded the whole of the , which was the second of the great commercial roads between the and .
Without saying anything to the captains of his fleet , who , without doubt , would have rebelled at the idea of attacking so strong a town , and the capital of a powerful empire , gave orders to double , and the fleet soon entered the of , the door of the , from whence was seen rising in all its magnificence a busy town built upon a rocky island , provided with formidable artillery , and protected by an army amounting to not less than from fifteen to twenty thousand men , while its harbour enclosed a fleet more numerous than could have been suspected at first sight .
At this sight the captains made urgent representations upon the danger that would run in attacking so well-prepared a town , and made the most of the plea how very bad an influence a reverse would exercise .
To this discourse answered , that indeed `` it was a very great affair , but that it was too late to draw back , and that he had greater need of determination than of good advice . ''
Scarcely was the anchor dropped before declared his ultimatum .
Although the forces under his orders were very disproportionate in numbers , the mõr imperiously demanded that should recognize the suzerainty of the King of and submit to his envoy , if it did not wish to share the same fate as .
The King , Seif-Ed-din , who was then reigning over , was still a child , and his Prime Minister , Kodja-Atar , a skilful and cunning diplomatist , governed in the king 's name .
Without denying in principle the pretensions of , the Prime Minister wished to gain time , to allow contingents to arrive for the help of the capital ; but the admiral , who guessed his object , did not hesitate , after waiting three days , to attack the formidable fleet at anchor under the guns of , with his five vessels and the la , the finest and largest ship of that time .
The combat was bloody and long undecided , but when they saw fortune was against them the , abandoning their vessels , endeavoured to swim on shore .
The upon this jumped into their boats , pursuing the Moors vigorously , and causing horrible carnage .
next directed his efforts against a large wooden jetty defended by numerous guns and by archers , whose well-aimed arrows wounded a number of the and the general himself , who , however , was not hindered thereby from landing and proceeding to burn the suburbs of the town .
Convinced that resistance would soon be impossible , and that their capital was in danger of being destroyed , the Moors hoisted a flag of truce , and signed a treaty , by which Seif-Ed-din declared himself the vassal of King Emmanuel , promised to pay him an annual tribute of 15,000 seraphins or xarafins , and gave to the conquerors a site for a fortress , which , in spite of the repugnance and reproaches of the captains , was soon put into a condition of resistance .
Unfortunately some deserters quickly brought these unworthy dissensions to the knowledge of Kodja-Atar , who profited by them to avoid , under various pretexts , fulfilling the execution of the articles of the new treaty .
Some days afterwards da and two other captains , jealous of the successes of , and trampling in the dust every sentiment of honour , discipline , and patriotism , left him to go to the ; while was obliged by this cowardly desertion to withdraw without being able even to guard the fortress which he had been at so much pains to construct .
He went to , where the garrison was in need of help , and then returned to cruise before , but thinking himself too weak to undertake anything , he retired for a time to , arriving there at the end of the year 1508 .
What had been occurring on the coast during this long and adventurous campaign ?
The answer may be summed up in a few lines .
It will be remembered that had set out from in 1505 with a fleet of twenty-two sail , carrying soldiers to the number of 1500 men .
First he seized and then , of which the `` cavaliers , as the inhabitants loved to repeat , did not yield as easily as the chicken hearts of . ''
Out of the enormous booty , which by the fall of this town fell into the hands of the , only took one arrow as his share of the spoil , thus giving a rare example of disinterestedness .
After having stopped at Melinda he went on to , where he delivered to the Rajah the golden crown sent to him by , whilst he himself , with the presumptuous vanity of which he gave so many proofs , assumed the title of viceroy .
Then , after commencing a fortress at , destined to overawe the of that coast , and his son , , scoured the , destroying the fleets , capturing some trading vessels , and causing great injury to the enemy , whose accustomed commercial roads were thus intercepted .
But for this cruising warfare a numerous fleet of light vessels was needed , for there was scarcely any other harbour of refuge except upon the coast .
How preferable was 's system of establishing himself in the country in a permanent manner , by constructing fortresses in all directions , by seizing upon the most powerful cities , whence it was easy to branch off into the interior of the country , by rendering himself master of the keys of the straits , and thus ensuring with much less risk , and more solidity , the monopoly of the commerce .
Meantime the victories of , and the conquests of had much disquieted the of .
The abandonment of the route caused a great diminution in the amount of imposts and dues of customs , anchorage , and transit , which were laid upon the merchandise of as it passed through his states .
Therefore , with the help of the Venetians , who furnished him with the wood for ship-building as well as with skilful sailors , he fitted out a squadron of twelve large ships , which came as far as , seeking the fleet of d'Almeida , and defeating it in a bloody combat in which was killed .
If the sorrow of the viceroy were great at this sad news , at least he did not let it appear outwardly , but set to work to make all preparations for taking prompt vengeance upon the , -- an appellation which shows the lasting terror attaching to the name of the , and commonly used at this time upon the coast , for all Mussulman soldiers coming from .
With nineteen sail appeared before the fort where his son had been killed , and gained a great victory , but one sullied , it must be confessed , by most frightful cruelties , so much so that it soon became a common saying : `` May the anger of the fall upon thee as it fell upon . ''
Not content with this first success , , some weeks later , annihilated the combined forces of the of , and the of , before Diu .
This victory made a profound impression in , and put an end to the power of the _Mahumetists_ of .
da and the other captains , who had abandoned before , had decided to rejoin ; they had excused their disobedience by calumnies , in consequence of which a judicial process was about to be instituted against , when the viceroy received the news of his being replaced in his office by .
At first declared that obedience must be rendered to this sovereign decree , but afterwards influenced by the traitors , who feared that they would be severely punished when the power had passed into the hands of , he repaired to in the month of March , 1509 , with the fixed determination not to give up the command to his successor .
There were disagreeable and painful disputes between these two great men , in which all the wrong done was on the side of .

The latter took the part of the prisoner , whom he immediately released , notifying again to Almeida the powers held by from the king , and threatening him with the great anger of if he refused to obey .

As for da , the author of these sad misunderstandings , he died some time afterwards , forsaken by everybody , and had scarcely any one to follow him to the grave except the new viceroy , who thus generously forgot the injuries done to .

In vain the new viceroy endeavoured to modify his zeal and induce him to take the wise measures recommended by experience .

On his return to , a sea-port which was a dependency of the King of , with whom the had been able to form an alliance , learnt that , the capital of a powerful kingdom , was a prey to political and religious anarchy .
Several chiefs were contending there for power .
One of them , , was just on the point of seizing the throne , and it was important to profit by the circumstances of the moment , and attack the town before he should have been able to gather a force capable of resisting the .
The viceroy perceived all the importance of this counsel .
The situation of , giving access as it did to the kingdom of and to the , had already struck him forcibly .
He did not delay , and soon the reckoned one conquest more .
Goa the , a cosmopolitan town , where were mingled with all the various sects of , the worshippers of , and even some Christians , submitted to , and soon became , under a wise and strict government which understood how to conciliate the sympathies of opposing sects , the capital , the chief fortress , and the principal seat of trade of the empire of the .
By degrees and with the course of years the knowledge of these rich countries had increased .
information had been gathered together by all those who had ploughed these sunny seas in their gallant vessels , and it was now known what was the centre of production of those spices which people went so far to seek , and for whose acquisition they encountered so many perils .
It was already several years since had founded the first factories in , the ancient Taprobane .
The of , and the of , were now exciting the desires of King Emmanuel , who had already been surnamed `` the fortunate . ''
He resolved to send a fleet to explore them , for had enough to do in to restrain the trembling , and the -- Moors as they were then called -- who were always ready to shake off the yoke .
This new expedition was under the command of , and according to the traditional policy of the , was at first amicably received at ; but when the suspicions of had been lulled to sleep by reiterated protestations of alliance , the whole population suddenly rose against him , and he was forced to return on board , but not without leaving thirty of his companions in the hands of the .
These events had already happened some time when the news of the taking of arrived at .
The _bendarra_ , or Minister of , who exercised regal power in the name of his nephew who was still a child , fearing the vengeance which the would doubtless exact for his treachery , resolved to pacify them .
He went to visit his prisoners , excused himself to them by swearing that all had been done unknown to him and against his will , for he desired nothing so much as to see the establish themselves in ; also he was about to order the authors of the treason to be sought out and punished .
The prisoners naturally gave no credence to these lying declarations , but profiting by the comparative liberty which was henceforth granted to them , they cleverly succeeded in conveying to some valuable information upon the position and strength of the town .
with much trouble collected a fleet of nineteen men of war , carrying fourteen hundred men , amongst whom there were only eight hundred .

In fact , it was impossible to reach in the teeth of the prevailing wind , while it was favourable for a descent upon .
This town , at that time in its full splendour , did not contain less than 100,000 inhabitants .
If many of the houses were built of wood , and roofed with the leaves of the palm-tree , yet they were equalled in number by the more important buildings , such as mosques and towers built of stone , which stretched out in a long panorama for the distance of three miles .
The ships of , , and of the kingdoms of the , met in its harbour , where numerous vessels coming from the coast , the , the , and the coast of traded in merchandise of all kinds and of every country .
When the of saw the fleet arrive in his waters , he felt that it was necessary to appear to give satisfaction to the foreigners by sacrificing the minister who had excited their anger and caused their arrival .
His ambassador therefore came to the viceroy to announce the death of the _bendarra_ , and to find out what were the intentions of the .
answered by demanding the prisoners who had remained in the hands of the , but the latter , desirous of gaining time to allow for the expected change in the trade-wind , -- a change which would force the to regain the coast , or else would oblige them to remain at , where he hoped to be able to exterminate them , -- invented a thousand pretexts for delay , and in the meantime according to the old narratives , he prepared a battery of 8000 cannon , and collected troops to the number of 20,000 .
At length lost his patience , and ordered some houses and several Gujerat vessels to be set on fire , a beginning of execution which speedily brought about the restoration of the prisoners ; he then claimed 20,000 crusades as indemnity for the damage caused to the fleet of , and finally he demanded to be allowed to build a fortress within the town itself , which should also serve as a counting-house for the merchants .
This demand could not be complied with as well knew ; but upon the refusal he resolved to seize the town , fixing upon ' day for the attack .
The town was taken quarter by quarter , house by house , after a truly heroic struggle and a most vigorous defence , which lasted for nine whole days , notwithstanding the employment of extraordinary devices , such as elephants of war , poisoned sabres and arrows , barricades , and skilfully concealed troops .
An enormous booty was divided amongst the soldiers , only reserving to himself six lions , of gold according to some accounts , of iron according to others , which he intended for the adornment of his tomb , to perpetuate the memory of his victory .
The door which gave access to , and to , was henceforth open .
Many nations unknown till this time would now have intercourse with .
The strange manners and fabulous history of many people were about to be disclosed to the astonished .
A new era had commenced , and these great results were due to the unbridled audacity , and indomitable courage of a nation whose country was scarcely discernible upon the map of the world !
It was in part owing to the religious toleration which displayed , a toleration which contrasts strangely with the cruel fanaticism of the , and in part to the skilful measures which he took , that the prosperity of resisted the rude shock which it had received .
In the course of a few months no trace remained of the trials which the town had experienced , except the sight of the banner floating proudly over this great city , which had now become the head and vanguard of the colonial empire of this people , small in numbers , but rendered great by their courage and their spirit of enterprise .
and wonderful as this new conquest might be , it had not made forget his former projects .
If he had appeared to have renounced them , it was only because circumstances had not hitherto seemed favourable for their execution .
With that tenacity of determination which formed the basis of his character , while still at the southern extremity of the empire which he was founding , his thoughts were fixed upon the northern part of it , upon , which the jealousy and treachery of his subordinates had obliged him to abandon at the beginning of his career , at the very moment when success was about to crown his persevering efforts ; it was which tempted him still .

The fame of his exploits and the terror inspired by his name had decided Kodja-Atar to make some advances to , to ask for a treaty , and to send the arrears of the tribute which had been formerly imposed .
Although the viceroy placed no belief on these repeated declarations of friendship -- on that faith which deserves to be as notorious as faith , -- he nevertheless welcomed them , whilst waiting for the power to establish his dominion after a permanent manner in these countries .
In 1513 or 1514 -- the exact date is not ascertained -- when his fleet and soldiers were set at liberty by the conquest of and the tranquillity of his other possessions , set sail for the .
Immediately upon his arrival , although a series of revolutions had changed the government of and the power was then in the hands of a usurper named Rais-Nordim or , demanded that the fortress , which had been formerly begun , should be immediately placed in his hands .
After having had it repaired and finished , he took part against the pretender , in the quarrel which was then dividing the town of and preparing it to fall under the dominion of .
He seized upon the town and bestowed it upon the aspirant who had accepted his conditions beforehand , and who appeared to to present the most solid guarantees of submission and fidelity .
Besides , it would not be difficult in the future to make this certain , for left in the new fortress a garrison perfectly able to bring Rais-Nordim to repentance for the slightest attempt at revolt , or the least desire of independence .
A well-known anecdote is related of this expedition to , but one which , even from its notoriety , we should be blamed for omitting .
When the King of sent to to demand the tribute which the sovereigns of had been in the habit of paying to him , gave orders that a quantity of bullets , cannon-balls and shells , should be brought from his ships , and showing them to the ambassadors he told them that such was the coin in which the King of was accustomed to pay tribute .
It does not appear that the ambassadors repeated their demand .
