With his usual wisdom , the viceroy did not wound the feelings of the inhabitants , who speedily returned to the town .
Far from squeezing all he could from them , as his successors were destined soon to do , he established an upright system of government which caused the name to be loved and respected .
At the same time that he was himself accomplishing these marvellous labours , had desired some of his lieutenants to explore the unknown regions to which access had been given by the taking of .
For this purpose he gave to and d'Abreu the command of a small squadron carrying 220 men , with which they explored the whole of the , , , , , , , & c. ; then being not far from the coast of they sailed back again to the north and arrived at the of and , which form part of the group .
After having made a voyage of more than 1500 miles amongst dangerous archipelagos strewn with rocks and coral reefs , and amidst populations often hostile , and after loading their ships there with cloves , nutmegs , sandal-wood , mace , and pearls , they set sail for in 1512 .
This time the veritable land of spices had been reached , it now only remained to found establishments there and to take possession of it definitely , which was not likely to be long postponed .
It has been often remarked that the rock is not far from the ; of this was destined to make experience , and his last days were to be saddened by unmerited disgrace , the result of calumnies and lies , and of a skilfully woven plot , which , although it succeeded in temporarily clouding his reputation with , has not availed to obscure the glory of this great man in the eyes of posterity .
Already there had been an effort made to persuade the king that the taking possession of had been a grave error ; its unhealthy climate must , it was said , decimate the population in a short time , but the king , with perfect confidence in the experience and prudence of his lieutenant , had refused to listen to his enemies , for which had publicly thanked him , saying , -- '' I think more is owing to King Emmanuel for having defended against the , than to myself for having twice conquered it . ''
But in 1514 had asked the king to bestow upon him as a reward for his services the title of of , and it was this imprudent step which gave an advantage to his adversaries .
d'Albergavia and , whom had sent as prisoners to after they had publicly declared themselves his enemies , had succeeded not only in clearing themselves from the accusation brought against them by the viceroy , but in persuading that he wished to constitute an independent duchy of which should be the capital , and they ended by obtaining his disgrace .
The news of the appointment of to the post of Captain-General of , reached as he was issuing from the of on his return to the coast , and at a time when he was suffering much from disease .
`` He raised his hands towards heaven , '' says M. F. , in his excellent History of , `` and pronounced these few words : Behold I am in disgrace with the king on account of my love to men , and with men on account of my love to the king .
thee , old man , to the , and prepare to die , for it behoves thine honour that thou shouldest die , and never hast thou neglected to do aught which thine honour demands . ''
, being arrived in the roadstead of , set in order the affairs of his conscience with the , caused himself to be clad in the dress of the Order of of which he was a commander , and then `` on Sunday the 16th of December , an hour before daybreak , he rendered up his soul to God .
Thus ended all his labours , without their having ever brought him any satisfaction . ''
was buried with great pomp .
The soldiers who had been the faithful companions of his wonderful adventures , and the witnesses of his manifold tribulations , disputed amidst their tears for the honour of carrying his remains to their last resting-place , which their commander had himself chosen .
The in their grief refused to believe that he was dead , declaring that he was gone to command the armies of the sky .
A letter of King has been comparatively lately discovered which proves that , although he were deceived for a time by the false reports of the enemies of , he soon discovered his mistake , and rendered him full and entire justice .
Unfortunately this letter of reparation never reached the unfortunate second Viceroy of the ; it would have sweetened his last moments , whereas he had the pain of dying in the belief that the sovereign for whose glory and the increase of whose power he had consecrated his life , had in the end proved ungrateful towards him .
`` With , '' says , `` all humanity and all justice disappeared from amongst the conquerors .
years after his death the would repair to the tomb of the great , to demand justice of him against the oppressions of his successors . ''
Many causes may be adduced as bringing about the rapid decay and dismemberment of that great colonial empire with which had enriched his country , and which even amidst its ruins has left ineffaceable traces upon .
With we may cite the distance and dispersion of the various factories , the smallness of the population of , but little suited to the wide extension of her establishments , the love of brigandage , and the exactions of a bad government , but beyond all , that indomitable national pride which forbade any mingling of the victors with the vanquished .
The fall of the colonial empire was hindered for a time by the influence of two heroic men , the first was de , who after having had the control of untold riches , remained so poor that he had not even the wherewithal to buy a fowl in his last illness ; and the second , , who once again gave the corrupt eastern populations an example of the most manly virtues , and of the most upright administration .
But after their time the empire began to drop to pieces , and fell by degrees into the hands of the and the , who in their turn were unable to preserve it intact .
All passes away , all is changed .
What can be said but to repeat the saw , in applying it to the case of empires , `` Life is but a dream '' ?

The letters and narratives of and his companions , especially those dwelling upon the large quantity of gold and pearls found in the recently discovered countries , had inflamed the imagination of eager traders , and of numbers of gentlemen who loved adventure .
On the 10th of April , 1495 , the government had issued an order allowing any one who might wish to do so , to go and discover new countries ; but this privilege was so much abused , and complained so bitterly of its trenching upon established rights , that the permission was withdrawn on the 2nd of June , 1497 , and four years later it became necessary to repeat the prohibition with more severe penalties attached to its infringement .
The effect of the royal decree was at once to produce a kind of general rush to the , and this was favoured by of , through whose hands passed all business connected with the Indies , and of whom had had so much reason to complain .
The admiral had but just left San-Lucar on his third voyage , when four expeditions of discovery were fitted out almost at the same moment , at the cost of some rich ship-owners , foremost among whom we find the and .
The first of these expeditions , which left the port of on the 20th of May , 1499 , consisted of four vessels , and was commanded by .
de la sailed with him as pilot ; was also on board , without any very clearly defined duties , but he would seem to have been astronomer to the fleet .

Before entering on a brief account of this voyage , we will glance for a few moments at the three men whom we have just named ; the last of the three especially , plays a most important part in the discovery of the , which received its name from him .
, born at about 1465 , and brought up in the household of the of , had gained his first experience in arms in the wars against the Moors .
enrolled him amongst the adventurers whom he recruited for his second voyage , when distinguished himself alike by his cool courage and his readiness in surmounting all difficulties .
What caused his complete rupture with remains a mystery ; it appears still more inexplicable when we think of the distinguished services that had rendered , especially in 1495 , at the battle of , when the Confederation was annihilated .
All we know is , that on 's return to he found shelter and protection with .
It is said even that the minister supplied him with the journal of the admiral 's last voyage , and the map of the countries which had discovered .
The first pilot employed by was de la Cosa , born probably at , in the country .
He had often sailed along the coast of before accompanying on his first voyage , while in the second expedition he filled the post of hydrographer ( _maestro de hacer cartas_ ) .
As specimens of 's talent in drawing maps may be mentioned two very curious ones still extant ; one showing all the territory that had been acquired in in 1500 , the other on vellum , and enriched with colour like the first , giving the discoveries made by and his successors .
The second pilot was , who had likewise sailed with on his voyage to .
As to , his duties were not , as we have said , very clearly defined , he was there to aid in making discoveries ( _per ajutare a discoprire_ , says the text of his letter to ) .
Born at on the 9th of March , 1451 , belonged to a family of distinction and wealth .
He had made mathematics , natural philosophy , and astrology ( as it was then called ) his special studies .
His knowledge of history and literature , judging from his letters , appears to have been somewhat vague and ill-digested .
He left in 1492 without any special aim in view , and went to , where he occupied himself at first in commercial pursuits .
We hear of him in acting as factor in the powerful trading house of his fellow countryman , .
As this house had advanced money to for his second voyage , it is not unlikely that had become acquainted with the admiral at this period of his career .
On 's death in 1495 , was placed by his heirs at the head of the financial department of the house .
Whether he may have been tired of a situation that he thought below his powers , or been seized in his turn with the fever for making new discoveries , or whether he hoped to make his fortune rapidly in the new countries reputed to be so rich ; whatever in short may have been the motive that actuated him , at least this we know , that he joined 's expedition in 1499 , this fact being so stated in 's deposition in the law-suit instituted by the with the heirs of .
The flotilla , consisting of four vessels , set sail on the 20th of May from , taking a south-westerly course , and in twenty-seven days the continent was sighted at the place which was named , because the houses being built upon piles reminded the beholders of .
, after some ineffectual attempts to hold intercourse with the natives , with whom he had several skirmishes , next saw the of ; after sailing about 250 miles to the east of the river Orinoco he reached the Gulf of , and entered a bay called the of , from the natives of that part being employed in the pearl fisheries .
Guided by the maps of , passed by the Dragon's-Mouth , which separates from the continent , and returned westward to .
Then , after touching at the , where he made a number of prisoners , whom he hoped to sell for slaves in , he was obliged to cast anchor at , in , on the 5th of September , 1499 .
, knowing 's courage and his restless spirit only too well , feared that he would introduce a new element of discord into the colony .
He therefore despatched with two caravels to inquire into his motives in coming to the island , and if necessary to prevent his landing .
The admiral 's fears were but too well grounded ; had scarcely landed before he had an interview with some of the malcontents , inciting them to a rising at , and to a determination to expel .
After some skirmishes , which had not ended to 's advantage , a meeting was arranged for him with , d'Escobar , and la Cosa , when they prevailed upon him to leave the island .
`` He took with him , '' says , `` a prodigious cargo of slaves , whom he sold in the market at for enormous sums of money . ''
He returned to in February , 1500 , where he had been preceded by and B. Roldan on the 18th of October , 1499 .
The most southerly point that had reached in this voyage was 4 degrees north latitude , and he had only spent fourteen weeks on the voyage of discovery , properly so called .
If we appear to have dwelt at some length upon this voyage , it is because it was the first one made by .
Some authors , for instance , and quite recently , , in his history of Henry the Navigator , assert that ' first voyage was in 1497 , and consequently that he must have seen the continent before , but we prefer to follow , who spent so many years in studying the history of the discovery of , in his opinion that 1499 was the right date , also M. Ed .
and M. Jules Codine , the latter of whom discussed this question in the of the for 1873 , _apropos_ of 's book .
`` If it were true , '' says , `` that had discovered the , yet the glory would not be his ; it belongs undoubtedly to the man who had the genius and courage to undertake the first voyage , to . ''
As says in his argument with , `` the glory is due only to the inventor . ''
But we agree with M. Codine when he says , `` How can we allow that there was an expedition in 1497 which resulted in the discovery of above 2500 miles of the coast-line of the mainland , when there is no trace of it left either among the great historians of that time , or in the legal depositions in connexion with the claims made by the heir of against the Government , in which the priority of the discoveries of each leader of an expedition is carefully mentioned , with the part of the coast explored by each ? ''
Finally , the authentic documents extracted from the archives of the de contratacion_ make it evident that was entrusted with the preparation of the vessels destined for the third voyage of at and at from the middle of , 1497 , till the departure of on the 30th of May , 1498 .
The narratives of the voyages of are very diffuse and wanting in precision and order ; the information they give upon the places he visited is so vague , that it might apply to one part of the coast as well as to another ; as to the localities treated of , as well as of the companions of , there are no indications given of a nature to aid the historian .
Not a single name is given of any well-known person , and the dates are contradictory in those famous letters which have given endless work to commentators .
says of them `` There is an element of discord in the most authentic documents relating to the navigator . ''
We have given an account of 's first voyage , which coincides with that of according to , who has compared the principal incidents of the two narratives .
asserts that , having started on the 10th of May , 1497 , entered the Gulf of on the 10th of June , coasted by and , sailed up the , and at the end of February , 1498 , doubled the Cape of .
After anchoring for thirty-seven days at the mouth of the , he returned to in October , 1498 .
If had really made this marvellous voyage , he would have far outstripped all the navigators of his time , and would have fully deserved that his name should be given to the newly-discovered continent , whose coast-line he had explored for so great a distance .
But nothing is less certain , and 's opinion has hitherto appeared to the best writers to offer the largest amount of probability .
made three other voyages .
identifies the first with that of , and M. d'Avezac with that of de ( 1499-1500 ) .
At the close of this latter year , di induced to enter the service of , King of , and he accomplished two more voyages at the expense of his new master .
On the first of these two voyages , he was no higher in command than he had been in his earlier ones , and only accompanied the expedition as one whose intimate acquaintance with all nautical matters might prove of service under certain circumstances .
During this voyage the ships coasted along the shores from to 52 degrees of south latitude .
The fourth voyage of was marked by the wreck of the flag-ship off the of de , which prevented the other vessels from continuing their voyage towards by way of the Cape of , and obliged the crews to land at ' , in .
This fourth voyage was unquestionably made with , but we are quite ignorant as to who was in command on the third voyage .
These various expeditions had not tended to enrich , while his position at the court was so far from satisfactory that he determined to re-enter the service of the King of .
By him he was made on the 22nd of March , 1508 .
There were some valuable emoluments attached for his advantage to this appointment , which enabled him to end his days , if not as a rich man , at least as one far removed from want .
He died at on the 22nd of February , 1512 , with the same conviction as , that he had reached the shores of .
is especially famous from the World having been named after him , instead of being called , as in all justice it should have been , but with this had nothing to do .
He was for a long time charged , though most unjustly , with impudence , falsehood , and deceit , it being alleged that he wished to veil the glory of and to arrogate to himself the honour of a discovery which did not belong to him .
This was an utterly unfounded accusation , for was both loved and esteemed by and his contemporaries , and there is nothing in his writings to justify this calumnious assertion .
Seven printed documents exist which are attributed to ; they are -- the abridged accounts of his four voyages , two narratives of his third and fourth voyages , in the form of letters , addressed to de , and a letter addressed to the same nobleman , relative to the discoveries in the Indies .
These documents , printed and bound up as small thin volumes , were soon translated into various languages and distributed throughout .
It was in the year 1507 that a certain Hylacolymus , whose real name was , first proposed to give the name of to the new part of the world .
He did so in a book printed at and called introductio_ .
In 1509 a small geographical treatise appeared at adopting the proposal of ; and in 1520 an edition of was printed at , giving a map of the World with the name of .
From this time the number of works employing the denomination proposed by increased perpetually .
Some years later , when was better informed as to the real discoverer of and of the value to be placed upon the voyages of , he eliminated from his book all that related to the latter , and substituted everywhere the name of for that of , but it was too late , the same error has prevailed ever since .
As to himself , it seems very unlikely that he was at all aware of the excitement which prevailed in , nor of what was passing at .
The testimony that has been unanimously borne to his honourable and upright conduct should surely clear him from the unmerited accusations which have for too long a time clouded his memory .
Three other expeditions left almost at the same time as that of .

After this expedition , so fruitful in results , voyages of discovery became rather less frequent for some years ; the Spaniards being occupied in asserting their supremacy in the countries in which they had already founded colonies .

Two years afterwards had travelled over the island and had subjugated the poor savages , by means of those terrible dogs which had been trained to hunt , and unaccustomed as the natives were to any hard work , he had forced them to toil in the mines .

The cruelty with which this unfortunate people was treated became more and more unbearable .
By means of a despicable ambush , seized the Queen of and 300 of her principal subjects , and at a given signal they were all put to the sword without there being any crime adduced against them .
`` For some years , '' says , `` the gold brought into the royal treasury of amounted to about 460,000 _pesos_ ( 2,400,000 livres of the currency of ) an enormous sum if we take into consideration the great increase in the value of money since the beginning of the sixteenth century . ''
In 1511 Diego conquered with 300 men , and here again were enacted the terrible scenes of bloodshed and pillage which have rendered the name so sadly notorious .
They cut off the thumbs of the natives , put out their eyes , and poured boiling oil or melted lead into their wounds , even when they did not torture them by burning them over a slow fire to extract from them the secret of the treasures of which they were believed to be the possessors .
It was only natural under these circumstances that the population rapidly decreased , and the day was not far off when it would be wholly exterminated .
To understand fully the sufferings of this race thus odiously persecuted , the touching and horrible narrative of must be read , himself the indefatigable defender of the .
In , the was made prisoner and condemned to be burnt .
When he was tied to the stake , a monk tried to convert him , promising him that if he would only embrace the faith , he would be at once admitted to all the joys of .
`` Are there any Spaniards in that land of happiness and joy of which you speak ? ''
`` Yes , '' replied the monk , `` but only those who have been just and good in their lives . ''
`` The very best among them can have neither justice nor mercy ! ''
said the poor cacique , `` I do not wish to go to any place where I should meet a single man of that accursed race . ''
Does not this fact suffice to paint the degree of exasperation to which these unfortunate people had been driven ?
And these horrors were repeated wherever the set foot !
We will throw a veil over these atrocities practised by men who thought themselves civilized , and who pretended that they wished to convert to , the religion pre-eminently of love and mercy , a race who were in reality less savage than themselves .

Two years later de and Pinzon sailing southwards towards the equinoctial line , advanced as far as the 40 degrees of south latitude , and found , to their surprise , that the continent extended on their right hand even to this immense distance .
They landed several times , and took formal possession of the country , but could not found any colonies there , on account of the small resources they had at their command .
The principal result of this voyage was the more exact knowledge which it gave of the extent of this part of the globe .

Such a discovery would have contented many a traveller , but went from one island to another , tasting the water of every stream that he met with , without the satisfaction of seeing his white hair again becoming black or his wrinkles disappearing .

It was in this way that he learnt the existence six suns away ( six days ' journey ) , of another sea , the , which washed the shores of , a country where gold was found in large quantities .

He assembled a body of 190 volunteers , all valiant soldiers , and like himself , accustomed to all the chances of war , as well as acclimatised to the unhealthy effluvia of a marshy country , where fever , dysentery , and complaints of the liver were constantly present .
Though the of is only sixty miles in width , it is divided into two parts by a chain of high mountains ; at the foot of these the alluvial soil is marvellously fertile , and the vegetation far more luxuriant than any can imagine .
It consists of an inextricable mass of tropical plants , creepers , and ferns , among trees of gigantic size which completely hide the sun , a truly virgin forest , interspersed here and there with patches of stagnant water , where live multitudes of birds , insects , and animals , never disturbed by the foot of man .
A warm , moist atmosphere exists here which exhausts the strength and speedily saps the energy of any man , even the most robust .
With all these obstacles which seemed to have rejoiced in placing in 's path , there was yet another no less formidable , and this was the resistance which the savage inhabitants of this inhospitable shore would offer to his progress .
set out without caring for the risk he ran in the event of the guides and native auxiliaries proving faithless ; he was escorted by a thousand Indians as porters , and accompanied by a troop of those terrible bloodhounds which had acquired the taste for human flesh in .
Of the tribes that he met with on his route , some fled into the mountains carrying their provisions with them , and others , taking advantage of the difficulties the land presented , tried to fight .
marching in the midst of his men , never sparing himself , sharing in their privations and rousing their courage , which would have failed more than once , was able to inspire them with so much enthusiasm for the object that was before them , that after twenty-five days of marching and fighting , they could see from the top of a mountain that vast , of which , four days later , , his drawn sword in one hand and the banner of in the other , took possession in the name of the King of .
The part of the which he had reached is situated to the east of , and still bears the name of the Gulf of , given to it by .
The information he obtained from the neighbouring caciques , whom he subjugated by force of arms , and from whom he obtained a considerable booty , agreed in every particular with what he had heard before he set out .
A vast empire lay to the south , they said , `` so rich in gold , that even the commonest instruments were made of it , '' where the domestic animals were llamas that had been tamed and trained to carry heavy burdens , and whose appearance in the native drawings resembled that of the camel .
These interesting details , and the great quantity of pearls offered to , confirmed him in his idea , that he must have reached the countries described by , and that he could not be far from the empire of or , of which the traveller had described the marvellous riches which were perpetually dazzling the eyes of these avaricious adventurers .

He set sail again after anchoring for four days , took a westerly course along the coast of , and on the 19th of May entered a river named by the natives the , where he soon found himself surrounded by a fleet of fifty native boats filled with warriors ready for the conflict , but thanks to 's prudence and the amicable demonstrations which he made , peace was not disturbed .
`` We made them understand , '' writes , `` that we were the subjects of a powerful emperor called , and that it would be greatly to their advantage if they also would acknowledge him as their master .
They replied that they had a sovereign already , and were at a loss to understand why we , who had only just arrived , and who knew so little of them , should offer them another king . ''
This reply was scarcely that of a savage !
In exchange for some worthless trinkets , the obtained some Yucca bread , copal gum , pieces of gold worked into the shape of fishes or birds , and garments made of cotton , which had been woven in the country .
As the natives who had been taken on board at did not perfectly understand the language spoken by the inhabitants of , the stay here was but of short duration , and the ships again put to sea .
They passed the mouth of the , the snowy peaks of the mountains being seen in the distance , and they anchored at the mouth of a river which was called de las Banderas_ , from the number of white banners displayed by the natives to show their friendly feeling towards the new comers .
When landed , he was received with the same honour as the paid to their gods ; they burnt copal incense before him , and laid at his feet more than 1500 piastres ' worth of small gold jewels , as well as green pearls and copper hatchets .
After taking formal possession of the country , the landed on an island called , from a sort of altar which they found there placed at the top of several steps , upon which lay the bodies of five Indians sacrificed since the preceding evening ; their bodies were cut open , their hearts torn out , and both legs and arms cut off .
Leaving this revolting spectacle , they went to another small island , which received the name of , being discovered on St. 's Day ; to this they added the word , which they heard used by the natives of these shores .

The results obtained from this voyage were considerable .
For the first time the long line of coast which forms the peninsula of , the of , and the base of the Gulf of , had been explored continuously from cape to cape .
Not only had it been proved beyond doubt that was not an island as they had believed , but much and reliable information had been collected with regard to the existence of the rich and powerful empire of .
The explorers had been much struck with the marks of a more advanced civilization than that existing in the , with the superiority of the architecture , the skilful cultivation of the land , the fine texture of the cotton garments , and the delicacy of finish of the golden ornaments worn by the .
All this combined to increase the thirst for riches among the of , and to urge them on like modern Argonauts to the conquest of this new golden fleece .

At the same time he fitted out a new armament proportioned to the dangers and importance of the undertaking that he proposed .
But though it was comparatively easy for to collect the necessary material and men , it was far more difficult for him -- whom an old writer describes as niggardly , credulous , and suspicious in disposition -- to choose a fit leader .
He wished indeed , to find one who should combine qualities nearly always incompatible , high courage and great talent , without which there was no chance of success , with at the same time sufficient docility and submissiveness , to do nothing without orders , and to leave to him who incurred no risk , any glory and success which might attend the enterprise .
Some who were brave and enterprising would not be treated as mere machines ; others who were more docile or more cunning lacked the qualities required to insure the success of so vast an enterprise ; among the former were some of 's companions who wished that he should be made commander , while the latter preferred Augustin Bermudez or .

As de was the governor 's secretary , he hastened to formulate the powers in a deed , making them very ample , as desired , and brought it to him duly signed . ''

was born at in in 1485 , of an ancient , but slenderly-endowed family ; after studying at for some time , he returned to his native town , but the quiet monotonous life there was little suited to his restless and capricious temper , and he soon started for , reckoning upon the protection of his relation , the Governor of .
His expectations were fully realized , and he held several honourable and lucrative posts , without counting that between times he joined in several expeditions against the natives .
If he became in this manner initiated into the system of tactics , so also , unfortunately , did he grow familiar with those acts of cruelty which have too often stained the name .
He accompanied de Velasquez in his expedition in 1511 , and here he distinguished himself so highly , that notwithstanding certain disagreements with his chief , a large grant of land as well as of was made to him as a recognition of his services .
amassed the sum of 3000 castellanos in the course of a few years by his industry and frugality , a large sum for one in his position , but his chief recommendations in the eyes of de and de his two patrons , were his activity , his well-known prudence , his decision of character , and the power of gaining the confidence of all with whom he was brought into contact .
In addition to all this , he was of imposing stature and appearance , very athletic , and possessed powers of endurance , remarkable even among the hardy adventurers who were accustomed to brave all kinds of hardships .
As soon as had received his commission , which he did with every mark of respectful gratitude , he set up a banner at the door of his house , made of black velvet embroidered in gold , bearing the device of a red cross in the midst of blue and white flames , and below , this motto in , `` Friends , let us follow the , and if we have faith , we shall overcome by this sign . ''
He concentrated the whole force of his powerful mind upon the means to make the enterprise a success ; even his most intimate friends were astonished at his enthusiasm in preparing for it .
He not only gave the whole of the money which he possessed towards arming the fleet , but he charged part on his estate , and borrowed considerable sums from his friends to purchase vessels , provisions , munitions of war , and horses .
In a few days 300 volunteers had enrolled themselves , attracted by the fame of the general , the daring nature of the enterprise , and the profit that would probably accrue from it .

When discovered that his plans had been check-mated he concealed his indignation , but at the same time , he made every arrangement to stop the man who could thus throw off all dependence upon him with such consummate coolness .

At length , having recalled the volunteers by beat of drum , and taken on board all that appeared necessary , set sail on the 18th February , 1519 , with eleven ships ( the largest being of 100 tons ) , 110 sailors , 553 soldiers , -- 13 of whom were arquebusiers , -- 200 Indians from the island , and some women for domestic work .
The real strength of the armament lay in the ten pieces of artillery , the four falconets provided with an ample supply of ammunition , and the sixteen horses which had been obtained at great expense .
It was with these almost miserable means , which , however , had given much trouble to collect , that he prepared to wage war with a sovereign whose dominions were of greater extent than those appertaining to the King of -- an enterprise from which he would have turned back if he had foreseen half its difficulties .
But long ago a poet said , `` Fortune smiles on those who dare . ''
After encountering a very severe storm , the fleet touched at the island of , where they found that the inhabitants had embraced Christianity , either from fear of the , or from finding the inability of their gods to help them .
Just as the fleet was about to leave the island , had the good fortune to meet with a named d'Aguilar , who had been kept a prisoner by the for eight years .
During that time he had learnt the language perfectly ; he was as prudent as he was clever , and when he joined the expedition he was of the greatest use as an interpreter .
After doubling , sailed down the of , passed , and entered the , hoping to meet with as friendly a reception there as had done , and also to collect an equally large quantity of gold ; but he found a great change had taken place in the feelings of the natives , and he was obliged to employ force .
In spite of the bravery and numerical superiority of the , the overcame them in several engagements , thanks to the terror caused by the reports of their fire-arms and the sight of the cavalry , whom the took for supernatural beings .
The lost a large number of men in these engagements , while among the Spaniards two were killed , and fourteen men and several horses wounded ; the wounds of the latter were dressed with fat taken from the dead bodies of the .
At last peace was made , and the natives gave provisions , some cotton clothing , a small quantity of gold , and twenty female slaves , among whom was the celebrated , who rendered such signal services to the as an interpreter , and who is mentioned by all the historians of the conquest of the .

To give these poor Indians an adequate idea of his power , called out his soldiers , and put them through their drill , he also ordered the discharge of some pieces of artillery , the noise of which froze the hearts of the savages with terror .
During the whole time of the interview , some painters had been employed in sketching upon pieces of white cotton , the ships , the troops , and everything which had struck their fancy .
These drawings very cleverly executed , were to be sent to .
Before beginning the history of the heroic struggles which shortly commenced , it will be useful to give some details as to that empire which , powerful as it appeared , nevertheless contained within itself numerous elements of decay and dissolution , which fact explains the cause of its conquest by a mere handful of adventurers .
That part of which was under the dominion of was called and lay between 14 degrees and 20 degrees north latitude .
This region presents great varieties of climate on account of its difference of altitude ; towards the centre , and rather nearer to the than to the , there is a huge basin at an elevation of 7500 feet above the sea , and about 200 miles in circumference , in the hollow of which there were at that time several lakes ; this depression is called the valley of , taking its name from the capital of the empire .
As may be easily supposed , we possess very few authentic details about a people whose written annals were burnt by the ignorant `` conquistadores '' and by fanatical monks , who jealously suppressed everything which might remind the conquered race of their ancient religious and political traditions .
Arriving from the north in the seventh century the had overspread the plateau of .
They were an intelligent race of people , addicted to agriculture and the mechanical arts , understanding the working in metals , and to whom is due the construction of the greater part of the sumptuous and gigantic edifices of which the ruins are found in every direction in .
After four centuries of power , the disappeared from the country as mysteriously as they had come .
A century later they were replaced by a savage tribe from the north-west , who were soon followed by more civilized races , speaking apparently the language .
The most celebrated of these tribes were the , and the or Tezcucans , who assimilated themselves easily with the tincture of civilization which remained in the country with the last of the .
The , after a series of migrations and wars , settled themselves in 1326 in the valley of , where they built their capital .
A treaty of alliance both offensive and defensive was entered into between the states of , , and , and was rigorously observed for a whole century ; in consequence of this the civilization , which had been at first bounded by the extent of the valley , spread on all sides , and soon was limited only by the and .
In a short time these people had reached a higher degree of civilization than any other tribe in the .
The rights of property were recognized in , commerce flourished there , and three kinds of coin in circulation provided the ordinary mechanism of exchange .
There was a well-organized police , and a system of relays which worked with perfect regularity , and enabled the sovereign to transmit his orders with rapidity from one end of the empire to the other .
The number and beauty of the towns , the great size of the palaces , temples , and fortresses indicated an advanced civilization , which presented a singular contrast to the ferocious manners of the .
Their polytheistic religion was in the highest degree barbarous and sanguinary ; the priests formed a very numerous body , and exercised great influence even over political affairs .
by side with rites similar to those of , such as baptism and confession , the religion presented a tissue of the most absurd and bloody superstitions .
The offering up of human sacrifices , adopted at the beginning of the 14th century , and used at first very sparingly , had soon become so frequent , that the number of victims immolated each year , and drawn chiefly from the conquered nations , amounted to 20,000 , while under certain circumstances the number was much larger .
Thus in 1486 , at the inauguration of the temple of , 70,000 captives perished in a single day .
The Government of was monarchical ; at first the imperial power had been carefully limited , but it had increased with the various conquests , and had become despotic .
The sovereign was always chosen out of the same family , and his accession was marked by the offering up of numerous human sacrifices .
The belonged to the sacerdotal caste , and in consequence his power received some unwonted development .
The result of his numerous wars had been the extension of his frontiers , and the subjugation of various nations ; these latter welcomed the Spaniards with eagerness , thinking that their dominion must surely be less oppressive and less cruel than that of the .
It is certain that if , with the large force which he had at his disposal , had fallen upon the Spaniards when they were occupying the hot and unhealthy shore of Vera-Cruz , they would have been unable , in spite of the superiority of their arms and discipline , to resist such a shock ; they must all have perished , or been obliged to re-embark , and the fate of the World would have been completely changed .
But the decision which formed the most salient point in the character of , was completely wanting in that of , a prince who never could at any time adopt a resolute policy .
ambassadors from the emperor had arrived at the camp , bringing to an order to quit the country , and upon his refusal all intercourse between the natives and the invaders had immediately ceased .
The situation was becoming critical , and this felt .
After having overcome some hesitation which had been shown by the troops , he laid the foundations of Vera-Cruz , a fortress designed to serve as a basis of operations , and a shelter in case of a possible re-embarkation .
He next organized a kind of civil government , a _junta_ , as it would be called in the present day , to which he resigned the commission which had been revoked by , and then he made the junta give him one with new provisions and more extended powers .
After this he received the envoys from the town of , who were come to solicit his alliance , and his protection against , whose dominion they bore with impatience .
was indeed fortunate in meeting with such allies so soon after landing , and not wishing to allow so golden an opportunity to slip , he welcomed the kindly , went with them to their capital , and after having caused a fortress to be constructed at on the sea-shore , he persuaded his new friends to refuse the payment of tribute to .
He took advantage of his stay at to exhort these people to embrace Christianity , and he threw down their idols , as he had already done at , to prove to them the powerlessness of their gods .
Meanwhile a plot had been forming in his own camp , and , feeling convinced that as long as there remained any way of returning to , there would be constant lukewarmness and discontent among his soldiers , caused all his ships to be run aground , under the pretext of their being in too shattered a condition to be of any further use .
This was an unheard-of act of audacity , and one which forced his companions either to conquer or to die .
Having no longer anything to fear from the want of discipline of his troops , set out for on the 16th of , with five hundred soldiers , fifteen horses , and six field cannon , and also two hundred porters , who were intended to perform all menial offices .
The little army soon reached the frontiers of the small republic of , of which the fierce inhabitants , impatient of servitude , had long been engaged in strife with .
flattered himself that his oft-proclaimed intention of delivering the Indians from the yoke would induce the Tlascalans to become his allies and at once to make common cause with him .
He therefore asked for leave to cross their territory on his way to ; but his ambassadors were detained , and as he advanced into the interior of the country , he was harassed for fourteen consecutive days and nights by continual attacks from several bodies of , amounting in all to 30,000 men , who displayed a bravery and determination such as the had never yet seen equalled in the .
But the arms possessed by these brave men were very primitive .
What could they effect with only arrows and lances tipped with obsidian or fish-bones , stakes hardened in the fire , wooden swords , and above all with an inferior system of tactics ?
When they found that each encounter cost them the lives of many of their bravest warriors , while not a single had been killed , they imagined that these strangers must be of a superior order of beings , while they could not tell what opinion to form of men who sent back to them the spies taken in their camp , with their hands cut off , and who yet after each victory not only did not devour their prisoners , as the would have done , but released them , loading them with presents and proposing peace .
Upon this the declared themselves vassals of the crown , and swore to assist in all his expeditions , while he on his side promised to protect them against their enemies .
It was time that peace should be made , for many of the were wounded or ill , and all were worn out with fatigue , but the entry in triumph into , where they were welcomed as supernatural beings , quickly made them forget their sufferings .
After twenty days of repose in this town , resumed his march towards , having with him an auxiliary army of six thousand Tlascalans .
He went first to , a town regarded as sacred by the , and as the sanctuary and favoured residence of their deities .
felt much satisfaction in the advance of the to this town , either from the hope that the gods would themselves avenge the desecration of their temples , or that he thought a rising , and massacre of the might be more easily organized in this populous and fanatical town .
had been warned by the Tlascalans that he must place no trust in the protestations of friendship and devotion made by the Cholulans .
However , he took up his quarters in the town , considering that he would lose his prestige if he showed any signs of fear , but upon being informed by the Tlascalans that the women and children were being sent away , and by that a considerable body of troops was massed at the gates of the city , that pitfalls and trenches were dug in the streets , whilst the roofs of the houses were loaded with stones and missiles , anticipated the designs of his enemies , gave orders to make prisoners of all the principal men of the town , and then organized a general massacre of the population , thus taken by surprise and deprived of their leaders .
For two whole days the unhappy Cholulans were subject to all the horrors which could be invented by the rage of the , and the vengeance of their allies the Tlascalans .
A terrible example was made , six thousand people being put to the sword , temples burned to the ground , and the town half destroyed , a work of destruction well calculated to strike terror into the hearts of and his subjects .
miles now separated from the capital , and everywhere as he passed along he was received as a liberator .
There was not a cacique who had not some cause of complaint against the imperial despotism , and felt confirmed in the hope that so divided an empire would prove an easy prey .
As the descended from the mountains of , they beheld with astonishment the valley of , with its enormous lake , deeply sunk and surrounded by large towns , the capital city built upon piles , and the well-cultivated fields of this fertile region .
did not trouble himself about the continued tergiversations of , who could not make up his mind to the last moment whether he would receive the as friends or enemies .
The general advanced along the causeway which leads to across the lake , and was already within a mile of the town , when some Indians , who , from their magnificent costume were evidently of high rank , came to greet him and to announce to him the approach of the emperor .
soon appeared , borne upon the shoulders of his favourites in a kind of litter adorned with gold and feathers , while a magnificent canopy protected him from the rays of the sun .
As he advanced the prostrated themselves before him , with their heads downwards , as though unworthy even to look at their monarch .
This first interview was cordial , and himself conducted his guests to the abode which he had prepared for them .
It was a vast palace , surrounded by a stone wall , and defended by high towers .
immediately took measures of defence , and ordered the cannon to be pointed upon the roads leading to the palace .
At the second interview , magnificent presents were offered both to the general and soldiers .
related that according to an old tradition , the ancestors of the had arrived in the country under the leadership of a man of white complexion , and bearded like the .
After laying the foundations of their power , he had embarked upon the ocean , promising them that one day his descendants would come to visit them and to reform their laws -- and if , as said , he now received the rather as fathers than as foreigners , it was because he felt convinced that in them he beheld the descendants of his people 's ancient chief , and he begged them to regard themselves as the masters of his country .
The following days were employed in visiting the town , which appeared to the as larger , more populous , and more beautiful than any city which they had hitherto seen in .
Its distinguishing peculiarity consisted in the causeways which formed a means of communication with the land , and which were cut through in various places to allow a free passage to vessels sailing on the waters of the lake .
Across these openings were thrown bridges which could be easily destroyed .
On the eastern side of the town there was no causeway and no means of communication with the land except by canoes .
This arrangement of the town of caused some anxiety to , who saw that he might be at any moment blockaded in the town , without being able to find means of egress .
He determined , therefore , to prevent any seditious attempt by securing the person of the emperor , and using him as a hostage .
The following news which he had just received furnished him with an excellent pretext : Qualpopoca , a general , had attacked the provinces which had submitted to the , and and seven of his soldiers had been mortally wounded ; besides this , a prisoner had been beheaded and the head carried from town to town , thus proving that the invaders could be conquered , and were nothing more than ordinary mortals .
profited by these events to accuse the emperor of perfidy .
He declared that although appeared friendly to him and to his soldiers , it was only that he might wait for some favourable opportunity to treat them in the same manner as , a proceeding quite unworthy of a monarch , and very different from the confidence which had shown in coming , as he had done , to visit him .
He went on to say that if the suspicions of the Spaniards were not justified , the emperor could easily exonerate himself by having punished , and finally , to prevent the recurrence of aggressions which could but destroy the existing harmony , and to prove to the Mexicans that he harboured no ill-design against the , could not do otherwise than come to reside amongst them .
It may be easily imagined that the emperor was not very ready to decide upon this course , but was at last obliged to give in to the violence and threats of the .
Upon announcing his resolution to his subjects , he was made to assure them several times over that he put himself into the hands of the of his own free will ; these words were needed to calm the , who threatened to make an attack upon the foreigners .
The success of in this bold scheme was quite beyond his expectations .
, with his son and five of the chief ringleaders in the revolt , were seized by the , and brought before a tribunal , which was at the same time judge and prosecutor ; the Indians were condemned and burnt alive .
Not content with having punished men who had committed no crime but that of executing the orders of their emperor , and of opposing an armed resistance to the invasion of their country , imposed a new humiliation upon , in placing fetters upon his feet , under the pretext that the culprits in their last moments had made accusations against him .
For six months the `` Conquistador '' exercised the supreme government in the name of the emperor , now reduced to a puppet-show of authority .
changed the governors who displeased him , collected the taxes , presided over all the details of the administration , and sent into the various provinces of the empire with orders to examine their productions , and to take particular notice of the mining districts and the processes in use for collecting gold .
also turned to account the curiosity evinced by to see ships , to have rigging and other appurtenances brought from Vera-Cruz , and to order the construction of two brigantines destined to ensure his communications with terra-firma by the waters of the lake .
Emboldened by receiving so many proofs of submission and humility , took another step in advance , and required that should declare himself the vassal and tributary of .
The act of fidelity and homage was accompanied , as may be easily imagined , with presents both rich and numerous , as well as by a heavy tax which was levied without much difficulty .
The opportunity was now taken to gather together everything in gold and silver , which had been extorted from the , and to melt them down , except certain pieces which were kept as they were , on account of the beauty of the workmanship .
The whole did not amount to more than 600,000 pesos , or 100,000_l._ Thus , although the had made use of all their power , and had exhausted his treasures to satisfy them , the whole product amounted to an absurdly small sum , very little in accordance with the idea which the conquerors had formed of the riches of the country .
After reserving one-fifth of the treasure for the king , and one-fifth for and subtracting enough to reimburse the sums which had been advanced for the expenses of the expedition , the share of each soldier did not amount to 100 _pesos_ , and they considered that it would have been more worth their while to have remained in , than to have experienced such fatigues , encountered such great dangers , and suffered so many privations , all for the reward of 100 _pesos_ !
If the promises of ended in this beggarly result , and if the partition had been made with fairness , of which they did not feel certain , they argued that it was absurd to remain longer in so poor a country , while under a chief less prodigal in promises , but more generous , they might go to countries rich in gold and precious stones , where brave warriors would find an adequate compensation for their toils .
So murmured these greedy adventurers ; some accepting what fell to their share while fuming over its small amount , others disdainfully refusing it .
had succeeded in persuading to conform to his will in everything which concerned politics , but it was otherwise in regard to religion .
He could not persuade him to change his creed , and when wished to throw down the idols , as he had done at , a tumult arose which would have become very serious , had he not immediately abandoned his project .
From that time the , who had offered scarcely any resistance to the subjugation and imprisonment of their monarch , resolved to avenge their outraged deities , and they prepared a simultaneous rising against the invaders .
It was at this juncture , when the affairs in the interior seemed to be taking a less favourable turn , that received news from Vera-Cruz , that several ships were cruising off the harbour .
At first he thought this must be a fleet sent to his aid by , in answer to a letter which he had sent to him on the 16th of July , 1519 , by and .
But he was soon undeceived , and learnt that this expedition was organized by , who knew by experience how lightly his lieutenant could shake off all dependence upon him ; he had sent this armament with the object of deposing from his command , of making him a prisoner , and of carrying him off to , where he would be speedily placed upon his trial .
The fleet thus sent was under the command of de Narvaez ; it consisted of eighteen vessels , and carried eighty horse-soldiers , and 100 infantry ( of whom eighty were musketeers ) , 120 cross-bowmen , and twelve cannons .
disembarked without opposition , near to the fort of d'Ulloa , but upon summoning the Governor of Vera-Cruz , , to give up the town to him , seized the men who were charged with the insolent message , and sent them off to , where at once released them , and then gained from them circumstantial information as to the forces , and the projects of .
The personal danger of at this moment was great ; the troops sent by were more numerous and better furnished with arms and ammunition than were his own , but his deepest cause of anxiety was not the possibility of his own condemnation and death , it was the fear lest all fruit of his efforts might be lost , and the knowledge of the hurtfulness of these dissensions to his country 's cause .
The situation was a critical one , but after mature reflection and the careful weighing of arguments for and against the course he meditated , determined to fight , even at a disadvantage , rather than to sacrifice his conquests and the interests of .
Before proceeding to this last extremity , he sent his chaplain to , but he was very ill-received , and saw all his proposals for an accommodation disdainfully rejected .
met with more success amongst the soldiers , who most of them knew him , and to whom he distributed a number of chains , gold rings , and other jewels , which were well calculated to give them a high idea of the riches of the conqueror .
But when heard of what was going on , he determined not to leave his troops any longer exposed to temptation ; he set a price upon the heads of and his principal officers , and advanced to the encounter .
, however , was too skilful to be enticed into giving battle under unfavourable circumstances .
He temporized and succeeded in tiring out and his troops , who retired to .
Then , having taken his measures with consummate prudence , and the surprise and terror of a nocturnal attack which he organized compensating for the inferiority of his troops , he made prisoners of his enemy and all his soldiers , his own loss amounting to but two men .
The conqueror treated the vanquished well , and gave them the choice between returning to , or remaining to share his fortune .
This latter proposal , backed up as it was by gifts and promises , appeared so seductive to the new arrivals , that found himself at the head of 1000 soldiers , the day after he had been in danger of falling into the hands of .
This rapid change of fortune was turned to the greatest advantage by the skilful diplomacy of , who hastened to return to .
The troops whom he had left there under the command of , to guard the emperor and the treasure , were reduced to the last extremity by the natives , who had killed or wounded a great number of soldiers , and who kept the rest in a state of close blockade , while threatening them constantly with a general assault .
It must be confessed that the imprudent and criminal conduct of the , and notably the massacre of the most distinguished citizens of the empire during a fête , had brought about the rising which they dreaded , and which they had hoped to prevent .
After having been joined by 2000 Tlascalans , pressed forward by forced marches towards the capital , where he arrived in safety , and found that the had not destroyed the bridges belonging to the causeways and dikes which joined to the land .
In spite of the arrival of this reinforcement , the situation did not improve .
Each day it was necessary to engage in new combats , and to make sorties to clear the avenues leading to the palace occupied by the .
now saw but too plainly the mistake which he had made in shutting himself up in a town where his position might be stormed at any moment , and from which it was so difficult to extricate himself .
In this difficulty he had recourse to , who , by virtue of his authority and of the prestige which still clung to him , could appease the tumult , give the Spaniards some respite , and enable them to prepare for their retreat .
But when the unfortunate emperor , now become a mere toy in the hands of the , appeared upon the walls decked out with regal ornaments , and implored his subjects to cease from hostilities , murmurs of discontent arose , and threats were freely uttered .
Hostilities began afresh , and before the soldiers had time to protect him with their shields , was pierced with arrows , and hit upon the head by a stone which knocked him down .
At this sight the , horrified at the crime which they had just committed , at once ceased fighting , and fled in all directions , while the emperor , understanding but too late all the baseness of the part which had forced him to play , tore off the bandages which had been applied to his wounds , and refusing all nourishment , he died cursing the .
After so fatal an event , there was no more room to hope for peace with the , and it became necessary to retire in haste , and at whatever cost , from a town in which the were threatened with blockade and starvation .
For this retreat was preparing in secret .
He saw his troops each day more and more closely hemmed in , whilst several times he was forced himself to take his sword in his hand and to fight like a common soldier .
even relates , but upon what authority is not known , that during an assault which was made upon one of the edifices commanding the quarter , two young Mexicans , recognizing , who was cheering on his soldiers , resolved to sacrifice themselves in the hope of killing the man who had been the author of their country 's calamities .
They approached him in a suppliant attitude , as though they would ask for quarter , then seizing him round the waist they dragged him towards the battlements , over which they threw themselves , hoping to drag him over with them .
But thanks to his exceptional strength and agility managed to escape from their embrace , and these two brave Mexicans perished in their generous but vain attempt to save their country .
The retreat being determined upon , it was necessary to decide upon whether it should be carried out by night or by day .
If in the daytime the enemy would be more easily resisted , any ambuscades which might be prepared would be more easily avoided , while they could better take precautions to repair any bridges broken by the .
On the other hand , it was known that the will seldom attack an enemy after sunset , but what really decided in favour of a nocturnal retreat was , that a soldier who dabbled in astrology had declared to his comrades that success was certain if they acted in the night .
They therefore began their march at midnight .
Besides the troops , had under his orders detachments from , , and , which , notwithstanding the serious losses which had been sustained , still numbered 7000 men .
commanded the vanguard , and Cortès the centre , where were the cannon , baggage , and prisoners , amongst whom were a son and two daughters of ; and de led the rearguard .
With the army was carried a flying bridge , which had been constructed to throw over any gaps there might be in the causeway .
Scarcely had the debouched upon the dike leading to , which was the shortest of all , when they were attacked in front , flank , and rear by solid masses of the enemy , whilst from a fleet of numberless canoes , a perfect hailstorm of stones and missiles fell upon them .
Blinded and amazed , the allies knew not against whom to defend themselves first .
The wooden bridge sank under the weight of the artillery and fighting men .
Crowded together upon a narrow causeway where they could not use their fire-arms , deprived of their cavalry who had not room to act , mingled with the Indians in a hand-to-hand combat , not having strength to kill , and surrounded on all sides , the and their allies gave way under the ever renewed numbers of the assailants .
Officers and soldiers , infantry and cavalry , and Tlascalans were confounded together , each defended himself to the best of his ability , without caring about discipline or the common safety .
All seemed lost , when with one hundred men succeeded in crossing the breach in the dike upon the mass of corpses which filled it up .
He drew up his soldiers in order as they arrived , and putting himself at the head of those least severely wounded , plunged wedge-fashion into the mêlée , and succeeded in disengaging from it a portion of his men .
Before day dawned all those who had succeeded in escaping from the massacre of the _noche triste_ , as this terrible night was called , found themselves reunited at .
It was with eyes full of tears that passed in review his remaining soldiers , all covered with wounds , and took account of the losses which he had sustained ; 4000 Indians , , and , and nearly all the horses were killed , all the artillery and ammunition , as well as the greatest part of the baggage , were lost , and amongst the dead were several officers of distinction -- de , , , , and many others ; one of those most dangerously hurt was , but not one man , whether officer or soldier , was without a wound .
The fugitives did not delay at , and by accident they took the road to , where they did not know what reception might await them .
Ever harassed by the , the Spaniards were again obliged to give battle upon the plains of to a number of warriors , whom some historians reckon at two hundred thousand .
to the presence of some cavalry soldiers who still remained to him , was able to overthrow all who were in front of him , and to reach a troop of persons whose high rank was easily discerned by their gilded plumes and luxurious costumes , amongst whom was the general bearing the standard .
Accompanied by some horsemen , threw himself upon this group and was fortunate enough , or skilful enough , to overturn by a lance-thrust the general , who was then despatched by the sword by a soldier named de .
From the moment when the standard disappeared the battle was gained , and the , panic-stricken , fled hastily from the field of battle .
`` Never had the Spaniards incurred greater danger , '' says , `` and had it not been for the lucky star of , not one would have survived to transmit to posterity the history of the sanguinary battle of . ''
The booty was considerable , and sufficed in part , to indemnify the for the loss they had sustained in leaving , for this army which they had just defeated was composed of the principal warriors of the nation , who , having been quite confident of success , had adorned themselves with their richest ornaments .

The day after the battle the entered the territory of .
says , `` I shall now call the attention of curious readers to the fact that when we returned to to the relief of , we were in all 1300 men , including in that number ninety-seven horsemen , eighty cross-bowmen , and the same number armed with carbines ; besides , we had more than 2000 Tlascalans , and much artillery .
Our second entry into took place on St. 's Day , 1520 ; our flight from the city was on the 10th day of the month of July following , and we fought the memorable battle of on the 14th day of this same month of July .
And now I would draw attention to the number of men who were killed at during the passage of the causeways and bridges , in the battle of , and in the other encounters upon the route .
I declare that in the space of five days 860 of our men were massacred , including ten of our soldiers and five women , who were killed in the village of ; we lost besides 1200 Tlascalans during the same time .
It is to be noticed also that if the number of dead in the troop of were greater than in the troop of , it was because the former soldiers set out on the march laden with a quantity of gold , the weight of which hindered them from swimming , and from getting out of the trenches . ''
The troops with were reduced to four hundred and forty men , with twenty horses , twelve cross-bowmen , and seven carabineers ; they had not a single charge of gunpowder , they were all wounded , lame , or maimed in the arms .
It was the same number of men that had followed when he first entered , but how great a difference was there between that conquering troop , and the vanquished soldiers who now quitted the capital .
As they entered the territory recommended his men , and especially those of , not to do anything which could vex the natives , the common safety depending upon not irritating the only allies which remained to them .
Happily the fears which had arisen as to the fidelity of the proved groundless .
They gave the Spaniards a most sympathizing welcome , and their thoughts seemed to be wholly bent upon avenging the death of their brothers massacred by the .
While in their capital heard of the loss of two more detachments , but these reverses , grave as they were , did not discourage him ; he had under his orders troops inured to war and faithful allies , Vera-Cruz was intact , he might once more reckon upon his good fortune .
But before undertaking a new campaign or entering upon another siege , help must be sought and preparations made , and with these objects in view the general set to work .
He sent four ships to to enrol volunteers and purchase powder and ammunition , and meanwhile he caused trees to be cut down in the mountains of , and with the wood thus obtained twelve brigantines were constructed , which were to be carried in pieces to the of , to be launched there at the moment when needed .
After suppressing some attempts at mutiny amongst the soldiers , in which those who had come with were the most to blame , again marched forwards , and , with the help of the Tlascalans , first attacked the people of and of other neighbouring provinces , a measure which had the advantage of exercising anew his own troops in war , and of training his allies .
While this was going on , two brigantines bringing ammunition and reinforcements fell into the hands of ; these ships had been sent to by , in ignorance of his misadventures ; at this time also some Spaniards sent by de , governor of , joined the army .
In consequence of these reinforcements the troops with , after he had rid himself of several partisans of with whom he was dissatisfied , amounted to five hundred infantry , of whom eighty carried muskets , and forty horse-soldiers .
With this small army , and with one thousand Tlascalans , set out once more for on the 28th of December , 1520 , six months after he had been forced to abandon the city .
This campaign had for its theatre countries already described , and must therefore be passed over somewhat rapidly here , notwithstanding the interest attaching to it ; to enter fully into the history of the conquest of would not be in accordance with the primary object of this work .
After the death of his brother was raised to the throne , and he adopted all the measures of precaution compatible with strategic science .
But he died of the smallpox , the sad gift of the to the , at the very moment when his brilliant qualities of foresight and bravery were the most needed by his country .
His successor was , the nephew of , a man distinguished by his talents and courage .
had no sooner entered the territory than fighting began .
He speedily captured the town of , which was situated at twenty miles ' distance , upon the edge of the great central lake , that lake upon whose waters the Spaniards were to see an imposing flotilla floating three months later .
At this time a fresh conspiracy , which had for its object the assassination of and his principal officers , was discovered , and the chief culprit executed .
At this moment fate seemed in every way to smile upon ; he had just received the news of the arrival of fresh reinforcements at Vera-Cruz , and the greater part of the towns under the dominion of had submitted to the force of his arms .
The actual siege of began in the month of May , 1521 , and continued with alternate success and reverse until the day when the brigantines were launched upon the water of the lake .
The Mexicans did not hesitate to attack them ; from four to five thousand canoes , each bearing two men , covered the lake and advanced to the assault of the vessels , which carried in all nearly three hundred men .
These nine brigantines were provided with cannon , and soon dispersed or sunk the enemy 's fleet , who thenceforth left them in undisputed possession of the water .
But this success and certain other advantages gained by had no very marked consequences , and the siege dragged slowly on , until the general made up his mind to capture the town by force .
Unfortunately the officer who was charged with protecting the line of retreat by the causeways while the Spaniards were making their way into the town , abandoned his post , thinking it unworthy of his valour , and went to join in the combat .
was informed of the fault which had been committed , and at once took advantage of it .
His troops attacked the Spaniards on all sides with such fury that numbers of them were killed in a short time , while sixty-two of the soldiers fell alive into the hands of the , a fate which , who was severely wounded in the thigh , narrowly escaped sharing .
During the night following , the great temple of the war-god was illuminated in sign of triumph , and the listened in profound sadness to the beating of the great drum .
From the position they occupied they could witness the end of the prisoners , their unfortunate countrymen , whose breasts were opened and their hearts torn out , and whose dead bodies were hurled down the steps ; they were then torn in pieces by the , who quarrelled over the pieces with the object of using them for a horrible festival .
This terrible defeat caused the siege to go on slowly , until the day came when three parts of the city having been taken or destroyed , was obliged by his councillors to quit and to set out for the mainland , where he reckoned upon organizing his resistance , but the boat which carried him being seized he was made prisoner .
In his captivity he was destined to display much greater dignity and strength of character than his uncle had done .
From this time all resistance ceased , and might take possession of the half-destroyed capital .
After a heroic resistance , in which 120,000 Mexicans according to some accounts , but 240,000 according to others , had perished , after a siege which had lasted not less than seventy days , , and with the city all the rest of the empire , succumbed , less indeed to the blows dealt against it by the Spaniards than to the long-standing hatred and the revolts of the subjugated people , and to the jealousy of the neighbouring states , fated soon to regret the yoke which they had so deliberately shaken off .
and rage soon succeeded amongst the to the intoxication of success ; the immense riches upon which they had reckoned either had no existence , or they had been thrown into the lake .
found it impossible to calm the malcontents , and was obliged to allow the emperor and his principal minister to be put to the torture .
Some historians , and notably , report that whilst the Spaniards were stirring the fire which burnt below the gridiron upon which the two victims were extended , the minister turned his head towards his master and apparently begged him to speak , in order to put an end to their tortures ; but that reproved this single moment of weakness by these words , `` And I , am I assisting at some pleasure , or am I in the bath ? ''
an answer which has been poetically changed into , `` And I , do I lie upon roses ? ''

The historians of the conquest of have usually stopped short at the taking of , but it remains for us to speak of some other expeditions undertaken by with different aims , but which resulted in casting quite a new light upon some portions of ; besides we could not leave this hero , who played so large a part in the history of the and in the development of its civilization , without giving some details of the end of his life .
With the fall of the capital was involved , properly speaking , that of the empire ; if there were still some resistance , as notably there was in the province of , it was of an isolated character , and a few detachments of troops sufficed to reduce to submission the last remaining opponents of the , terrified as the Mexicans were by the punishments which had been dealt out to the people of , who had revolted .
At the same time ambassadors were sent by the people of the distant countries of the empire , to convince themselves of the reality of that wonderful event , the taking of , to behold the ruins of the abhorred town , and to tender their submission to the conquerors .
was at length confirmed in the position he held after incidents which would take too long to relate , and which caused him to say , `` It has been harder for me to fight against my countrymen than against the . ''
It now remained to him to organize the conquered country , and he began by establishing the seat of government at , which he rebuilt .
He attracted to the city by granting them concessions of lands , and the , by allowing them at first to remain under the authority of their native chiefs , although he speedily reduced them all , except the Tlascalans , to the condition of slaves , by the vicious system of _repartimientos_ , in vogue in the colonies .
But if it is justifiable to reproach with having held cheaply the political rights of the , it must be conceded that he manifested the most laudable solicitude for their spiritual well-being .
To further this object he brought over some Franciscans , who by their zeal and charity in a short time gained the veneration of the natives , and in a space of twenty years brought about the conversion of the whole population .
At the same time sent some troops into the state of , who penetrated as far as the , and as they returned visited some of the rich provinces situated in the north .
