Immediately after the pacification of the country , entrusted de with the command of a considerable force , in order to establish a colony in , and at the same time was to explore the southern coast of that province , and to seek for a strait which should form a communication between the and .
But , carried away by the pride of command , had no sooner reached his destination than he declared himself independent , whereupon Cortès immediately despatched one of his relations to arrest the culprit , and set out himself , accompanied by , at the head of one hundred horsemen and fifty foot-soldiers , on the 12th of October , 1524 .
After crossing the provinces of , , and , and enduring all kinds of privations in the course of a most trying march over marshy and shifting ground , and across a perfect ocean of undulating forests , the detachment was approaching the province of , when was told of the existence of a plot , formed , as was said , by and the principal chiefs .
Its aim was to seize the first opportunity to massacre both officers and soldiers , after which the march to was to be continued , the settlements were to be destroyed , and then there was to be a return to , where during a general rising there would doubtless be small difficulty experienced in getting rid of the invaders .

del says , `` The execution of was very unjust , and we were all agreed in condemning it . ''
But says , `` If had consulted but his own interest and his renown , he should have spared him , for he was the living trophy of his victory , as a man keeps gold in the lining of his coat . ''

He reduced to submission the provinces of , , , , and laid the foundations of the town of la Vieja ; when , some time afterwards he made a voyage to , he was named by governor of the countries which he had conquered .
Three years had not expired after the conquest , before a territory 1200 miles in length upon the sea-board of the , and 1500 miles upon that of the , had submitted to the crown , and with but few exceptions , was in a state of perfect tranquillity .
The return of to from the useless expedition to -- which had wasted so much time and caused almost as great sufferings to the as the conquest of -- had taken place but a few days , when he received the news that he was temporarily replaced by another commander , and was invited to repair to to exculpate himself from certain charges .
He was not in any haste to comply with this order , hoping that it might be revoked , but his indefatigable calumniators and his implacable enemies , both in and , preferred accusations against him after such a manner , that he found himself obliged to go and make his defence , to state his wrongs , and boldly to claim the approval of his conduct .

The mere announcement of his return had produced a complete change in public opinion .
His unexpected arrival at once contradicted the idea that he harboured any projects of revolt and independence .
V. saw that public feeling would be outraged at the thought of punishing a man who had added its greatest gem to the crown of , and so the journey of became one continual triumph in the midst of crowds of people greater than had been ever known before .
`` The houses and streets of the large towns and of the villages , '' says , `` were filled with spectators impatient to contemplate the hero whose single arm might be said , in some sort , to have conquered an empire for , and who , to borrow the language of an old historian , marched in all the pomp and glory , not of a great vassal , but of an independent monarch . V. , after having granted several audiences to , and bestowed upon him those particular marks of favour which are termed important by courtiers , deigned to accept from him the empire which he had conquered for him , and the magnificent presents which he brought .
But he considered that he had fully recompensed him when he had given Cortès the title of della , and the post of captain-general of , without , however , restoring to him the civil government , a power which had been formerly delegated to him by the junta of Vera-Cruz .

After his arrival he underwent some annoyance caused by the , which had exercised the power in his absence , and which had instituted law-suits against him , and he also found himself in conflict with the new civil junta on the subject of military affairs .
The della withdrew himself to , where he had immense estates , and busied himself with agriculture .
He was the means of introducing the sugar-cane and the mulberry into , he also encouraged the cultivation of hemp and flax , and the breeding , on a large scale , of merino sheep .
But this peaceable life without adventures could not long satisfy the enterprising spirit of .
In 1532 and 1533 , he equipped two squadrons destined to make voyages of discovery in the north-west of the .
The latter expedition reached the southern extremity of the peninsula of without attaining the object sought , namely the discovery of a strait uniting the with the .

From thence the chief of the expedition sent back one of his ships to , while the rest proceeded northwards , but from that time nothing more is heard of them .

The whole of the , or Sea of , as the justly named it , was carefully explored , and it was ascertained that , instead of having an outlet as was supposed to the north , it was in reality only a gulf deeply hollowed into the continent .

But this journey was not destined at all to resemble the first .
old , disgusted with life , and betrayed by fortune , the `` conquistador '' had no longer anything to expect from government .
He had not to wait long before receiving proof of this ; one day he pressed through the crowd which surrounded the emperor 's coach , and mounted upon the step of the door .
V. pretended not to recognize him , and asked who this man was .
answered proudly , `` It is the man who has given you more States than your father left you Towns . ''
By this time public interest was diverted from , which had not yielded as much as had been expected from it , and was centred upon the marvellous riches of .

In 1541 , during the disastrous expedition of against , , who was serving in it as a volunteer , but whose counsels had not been listened to , had the misfortune to lose three great carved emeralds , jewels which would have sufficed for the ransom of an empire .
Upon his return he renewed his solicitations , but with the same want of success .
His grief over this injustice and these repeated disappointments was so deep , that his health suffered severely ; he died far from the scene of his exploits , on the 10th of November , 1547 , at de la , at the very moment when he was making preparations to return to .
`` He was a true knight errant , '' says ; `` of all that glorious troop of adventurers which the of the sixteenth century sent forth to a career of discovery and conquest , there was not one more deeply imbued with the spirit of romantic enterprise than .
was his delight , and he loved to attempt an enterprise by its most difficult side . `` ...
This passion for the romantic might have reduced the conqueror of to the part of a common adventurer , but was certainly a profound politician and a great captain , if one is justified in giving this name to a man who accomplished great actions by his own unassisted genius .
There is no other example in history of so great an enterprise having been carried to a successful end with such inadequate means .
It may be said with truth that conquered with his own resources alone .
His influence over the minds of his soldiers was the natural result of their confidence in his ability , but it must be attributed also to his popular manners , which rendered him eminently fit to lead a band of adventurers .
When he had attained to a higher rank , if displayed more of pomp , his veterans at least continued on the same terms of intimacy with him as before .
In finishing this portrait of the `` conquistador , '' we shall quote the upright and veracious , with whose sentiments we fully agree .
`` He preferred his name of to all the titles by which he might be addressed , and he had good reasons for it , for the name of is as famous in our days as that of amongst the , or Hannibal amongst the Carthaginians . ''
The old chronicler ends by a touch which vividly depicts the religious spirit of the sixteenth century : `` Perhaps he was destined to receive his reward only in a better world , and I fully believe it to be so ; for he was an honest knight , very sincere in his devotions to the , to the , and to all the saints . ''

The information which had been gained by as to the riches of the countries situated to the south of had scarcely become known to the before several expeditions were organized to attempt the conquest of them .
But all had failed , either from the means used being insufficient , or from the commanders not being equal to the greatness of the undertaking .
It must be confessed also that the localities explored by these first adventurers -- these pioneers , as they would be called now-a-days -- did not at all come up to what greed had expected from them , and for this reason , that all the attempts had been hitherto made upon what was then called `` , '' a country pre-eminently unhealthy , mountainous , marshy , and covered with forests ; the inhabitants were few , but of so warlike a disposition that they had added another obstacle to all those which nature had strewn with so prodigal a hand in the path of the invaders .
by little , therefore , the enthusiasm had cooled , and the wonderful narratives of were mentioned only to be turned into ridicule .
There lived , however , in a man well able to weigh the truth of the reports which had been circulated concerning the richness of the countries bathed by the ; this man was , who had accompanied de to the southern sea , and who now associated with himself two other adventurers , de and .
A few words must be said about the chiefs of the enterprise .

The young enlisted , and after passing some years amidst the wars , he followed to in 1510 .

The terms of partnership were soon agreed upon between these three men , of whom two at least were without fear , if they were not all three without reproach .

It was he who took the command of the first attempt , upon which we shall dwell in some detail , because it was then that the perseverance and inflexible obstinacy of the `` conquistador '' first came fully into sight .
One of the historians of the conquest of , de , relates as follows : -- '' Having then asked and obtained the permission of d'Avila , after much trouble equipped a vessel upon which he embarked with 140 men .
At the distance of 150 miles from Panama he discovered a small and poor province named , which caused the same name to be henceforward improperly bestowed upon all the country which was discovered along that coast for the space of more than 3600 miles in length .
Passing onwards he discovered another country , which the called _the burnt people_ .
The slew so many of his men that he was constrained to retire in great disorder to the country of , which is not far distant from the place whence he had started .

Not having met with , he went back northwards as far as _the burnt people_ , where , having ascertained by certain indications that had been there , he landed his men .
But the , puffed up by the victory which they had gained over , resisted bravely , forced the entrenchments with which had covered his position , and obliged him to re-embark .
He returned therefore , still following the coast-line until he arrived at , where he found .
They were much rejoiced at meeting again , and having added to their followers some fresh soldiers whom they had levied , they found their troops amounted to 200 Spaniards , and once more they descended the coast .
They suffered so much from scarcity of provisions and from the attacks of the , that returned to to collect more recruits and to obtain provisions .
He took back with him eighty men , with whom and with those who remained to them , they went as far as the country called , a country moderately peopled and where they found abundance of provisions .
They noticed that the Indians of these parts who attacked them and made war against them , had their faces studded with nails of gold inserted in holes which they had made expressly for receiving these ornaments .
de returned once again to , whilst his companion waited for him and for the reinforcements which he was to bring with him , in a small island called , where he suffered much from the scarcity of all the necessaries of life . ''

Upon his arrival in , could not obtain permission from , the successor of , to make new levies , for he had no right , said , to allow a greater number of people to go and perish uselessly in a rash enterprise ; he even sent a boat to to bring away and his companions .
But such a decision could not be pleasing to and .
It meant expense thrown away ; and it meant the annihilation of the hopes which the sight of the ornaments of gold and silver of the inhabitants of had caused them to entertain .
They sent therefore a trusty person to , to recommend him to persevere in his resolution , and to refuse to obey the orders of the Governor of .
But in vain held out the most seductive promises ; the remembrance of the fatigues which had been endured was too recent , and all his companions except twelve abandoned him .
With these intrepid men , whose names have been preserved , and amongst whom was de , one of the historians of the expedition , retired to an uninhabited island at a greater distance from the coast , to which he gave the name of .
There the lived miserably on mangles , fish , and shell-fish , and awaited for five months the succour that and were to send them .
At length , vanquished by the unanimous protestations of the whole colony , -- who were indignant that people whose only crime was that they had not despaired of success , should be left to perish miserably and as though they were malefactors , -- sent to Pizarro a small vessel to bring him back .
With the object of presenting no temptation to to make use of this ship to renew his expedition , not a single soldier was placed on board of her .
At the sight of the help which had arrived , and oblivious of all their privations , the thirteen adventurers thought of nothing but persuading the sailors who came to seek them to participate in their own hopes .
, instead of starting again on the route to , they sailed all together , towards the south-east , in spite of contrary winds and currents , until , after having discovered the of , they arrived at the port of , situated beyond the 3 degrees of south latitude , where they saw a magnificent temple and a palace belonging to the , the sovereigns of the country .
The country was populous and fairly well-cultivated , but what proved beyond all else seductive to the , and made them think that they had reached the marvellous countries of which so much had been said , was the sight of so great an abundance of gold and silver , that these metals were employed not only as finery and ornament by the inhabitants , but also for making vases and common utensils .
caused the interior of the country to be explored by de and , who brought back an enthusiastic description of it , and he caused some gold vases to be given up to him , as well as some llamas , a quadruped domesticated by the Peruvians .
He took two natives on board his vessel , to whom he proposed to teach the language , and to use them as interpreters when he should return to the country .
He anchored successively at , , and in the of Santa-Cruz , of which the sovereign , , received the strangers with such friendly demonstrations , that several of them were unwilling to re-embark .

He painted the picture of the countries that were to be conquered in the most pleasing light , and as a reward for his labours the titles of governor , captain-general , and alguazil-major of were bestowed upon him and his heirs in perpetuity .
At the same time he was ennobled , and a pension of 1000 crowns was bestowed upon him .
His jurisdiction , independent of the governor of , was to extend over a tract of 600 miles along the coast to the south of the river ; it was to be called , and he was to be the governor ; concessions that cost nothing to , for had yet to conquer the country .
On his side he undertook to raise a body of 250 men , and to provide himself with the necessary ships , arms , and ammunition .
then repaired to , where he persuaded his three brothers , , and to accompany him , as well as one of his half-brothers d'Alcantara .
He took advantage of his stay in his native town , and at , to try to raise recruits , both there and throughout ; they did not , however , come forward in large numbers , in spite of the title of _Caballeros de la dorada_ which he promised to bestow upon all who would serve under him .
Then he returned to , where affairs were not going so smoothly as he had hoped .
He had succeeded in getting named _protector de los ; but for , whose talents he knew , and whose ambition he feared , he had only asked that he should be ennobled and a gratuity of 500 ducats bestowed upon him , with the government of a fortress which was to be built at .
refused to take part in this new expedition ; he was not pleased with the meagre portion given to him after spending all his money on the earlier expeditions ; he wished now to organize one on his own account .
It required all 's address , aided by the promise to give up to Almagro the office of _adelantado_ , to appease him and make him consent to renew the old partnership .
The resources of the three partners were so limited at this time , that they could only get together three small ships and 124 soldiers , of whom thirty-six were horse-soldiers ; the expedition set out in February , 1531 , under the command of and his four brothers , whilst remained at to organize an expedition of supplies .
At the end of thirteen days ' sailing , and after having been carried by a storm 300 miles more to the south than he had intended , was forced to disembark both men and horses on the shores of the of , and to follow the line of the coast on land .
This march was a difficult one in a very mountainous country , thinly-peopled , and intersected by rivers which had to be crossed at their mouths .
At last a place called was reached , where was found a great booty , which decided to send back two of his ships .
They carried to and spoils to the amount of 30,000 _castellanos_ , as well as a great number of emeralds , a rich booty , which would , according to , determine many adventurers to come and join him .
Then the conqueror continued his march southwards as far as , where he was joined by and , who brought him twelve horsemen and thirty foot-soldiers .
The effect which had been produced in by the sight of the horses and the reports of the fire-arms was repeated in , and was able to reach the of in the Gulf of without encountering any resistance .
But the islanders were more numerous and more warlike than their brothers of the mainland , and for six months they valiantly resisted all the attacks of the .
Although had received some aid from , brought by , and although he had beheaded the cacique and sixteen of the principal chiefs , he could not overcome their resistance .
He was , therefore , obliged to regain the continent , where the maladies peculiar to the country tried his companions so cruelly , that he was forced to stay three months at , exposed to the perpetual attacks of the natives .
From Tumbez he went next to the , discovered the harbour of , the best on this coast , and founded the colony of San-Miguel , at the mouth of the , in order that vessels coming from might find a safe shelter .
It was here that received some envoys from , who informed him of the revolt of , the brother of , and asked his aid .
At the period when the landed to conquer , it extended along the shore of the for 1500 miles , and stretched into the interior as far as the imposing chain of the Andes .
Originally the population was divided into savage and barbarous tribes , having no idea of civilization , and living in a perpetual state of warfare with one another .
For many centuries affairs had continued in the same state , and there appeared no presage of the coming of a better era , when , on the shores of , there appeared to the Indians a man and woman , who pretended that they were the of the .
They called themselves Manco-Capac and Mama-Oello , and were of majestic appearance ; according to la Vega , towards the middle of the twelfth century they united together a number of wandering tribes , and laid the foundations of the town of .
Manco-Capac had taught the men agriculture and mechanical arts , whilst Mama-Oello instructed the women in spinning and weaving .
When Manco-Capac had satisfied these first needs of all societies , he framed laws for his subjects , and constituted a regular political state .
It was thus that the dominion of the or Lords of was established .
At first their empire was limited to the neighbourhood of , but under their successors it rapidly increased , and extended from the Tropic of to the , a length of thirty degrees .
The power of the incas was as absolute as that of the ancient sovereigns .
`` Also , '' says , `` there was perhaps no other country in the world where the obedience and submission of the subjects was carried further .
The incas were to them quasi-divinities ; they had but to place a thread drawn from the royal head-fillet in the hands of any one , and the man so distinguished , was certain to be everywhere respected and obeyed , and to find such absolute deference paid to the king 's order which he carried , that he could alone exterminate a whole province without any assistance from soldiers , and cause to be put to death all the inhabitants , both male and female , because at the mere sight of this thread , taken from the royal crown , the people voluntarily and without any resistance , offered themselves up to die . ''
However , the old chroniclers all agree in saying that this unlimited power was always used by the incas for the well-being of their subjects .
Out of a series of twelve kings , who in succession sat on the throne of , there was not one who did not leave behind him the memory of a just prince adored by his subjects .
Should we not search in vain through the annals of any other country in the world for facts analogous to these ?
Must it not be regretted that the should have brought war with all its attendant horrors , and the maladies and vices of a different climate , along with what they in their pride called civilization , amongst a rich and happy people , whose descendants , impoverished and debased as they are , have not even the recollection of their ancient prosperity to console them in their irremediable decay ?
`` The Peruvians , '' says in his admirable _Précis d'Histoire , `` handed down the principal facts to posterity by knots , which they made in ropes .
They had obelisks and exact gnomons to mark the equinoxes and solstices .
Their year consisted of 365 days .
They had erected prodigies of architecture , and they carved statues with amazing art .
They formed the most polished and industrious nation of the . ''
The inca Huayna-Capac , father of , under whom this vast empire was destroyed , had done much to increase and embellish it .
This inca , who conquered all the country of , had made , by the hands of his soldiers and of the vanquished people , a great road 1500 miles in length from to , across precipices which had been filled up and mountains which had been levelled .
Relays of men , stationed at intervals of a mile and a half from each other , carried the emperor 's orders throughout the empire .
was their police , and if we wish to judge of magnificence , we need only instance the fact that the king when he travelled was carried on a throne of gold which weighed 25,000 ducats , and the golden litter upon which the throne rested was borne by the highest personages of the realm .
In 1526 , when the appeared on the coast for the first time , the twelfth inca had lately married -- in defiance of the ancient law of the kingdom -- the daughter of the vanquished king of , and had had a son of this marriage named , to whom he left this kingdom on his death , which happened about 1529 .
His eldest son , whose mother was descended from the incas , had the remainder of his states .
But this partition , so contrary to the customs established from time immemorial , caused such great discontent at , that , encouraged by his subjects , determined to march against his brother , who would not acknowledge him for his lord and master .
, in his turn , had too lately tasted power to be willing to abandon it .
He managed by bribes to attach to himself the greater part of the warriors who had accompanied his father during the conquest of , and when the two armies met , fortune favoured the usurper .
Is it not curious to remark how both in and the were aided by entirely exceptional circumstances ?
In some of the people who had recently submitted to the race , being mercilessly trampled upon by their conquerors , welcome the as deliverers ; in Peru the strife between two brothers , furious against each other , hinders the Indians from turning all their forces against the invaders whom they might easily have crushed .
upon receiving the envoys sent by , to ask his aid against his brother , whom he represented as a rebel and usurper , saw at once all the advantages that might accrue to him from these circumstances .
He saw that by espousing the cause of one of the brothers , he could more easily crush them both , therefore he advanced at once into the interior of the country , at the head of a very inconsiderable force , consisting of sixty-two cavalry and one hundred and twenty foot-soldiers , of whom only twenty were armed with arquebuses and muskets ; he was obliged to leave part of his troops to guard San-Miguel , in which reckoned upon finding a refuge in case of his being unsuccessful , and where in any case all supplies which might arrive could be landed .
first made for , a small town situated at about twenty days ' march from the coast .
To reach it he had to cross a desert of burning sand , without vegetation and without water , which extended for sixty miles in length as far as the province of , and where the slightest attack of the enemy , joined to the sufferings endured by the little army , would have been sufficient to crush the whole expedition at one blow .
Next the troops plunged into the mountains and became entangled in narrow defiles where a small force might have annihilated them .
During this march received an envoy from bringing him some painted shoes and gold bracelets , which he was requested to wear at his approaching interview with the inca .
Naturally was lavish in his promises of friendship and devotion , and assured the ambassador that he should be only following the orders given him by the king his master in respecting the lives and property of the inhabitants .
From the moment of his arrival at prudently lodged his soldiers in a temple and a palace belonging to the inca , where they were sheltered from any surprise .
Then he sent one of his brothers with and twenty horse-soldiers to the camp of , which was distant only three miles , to announce to him his arrival .
The envoys of the governor were received with magnificence , and were astonished at the multiplicity of the ornaments and vases made of gold and silver which they saw throughout the camp .
They returned , bringing a promise from that he would come on the next day to visit , to bid him welcome to his kingdom .
At the same time the envoys gave an account of the wonderful riches they had seen , which confirmed in the project which he had formed of seizing the unfortunate Atahualpa and his treasures by treachery .
Several authors , and notably , disguise these facts , which no doubt appeared to them too odious , and altogether deny the treachery towards .
But at the present day there are extant many documents which force the historian to believe , with and , in the perfidy of .
It was very important for him to have the inca in his own hands , and to employ him as a tool , just as had done with .
He therefore took advantage of the honesty and simplicity of , who placed entire confidence in 's protestations of friendship and so was thrown off his guard , to arrange an ambuscade into which was certain to fall .
There was not a scruple in the disloyal soul of the conqueror ; he was as cool as though he were about to offer battle to enemies who had been forewarned of his approach ; this infamous treason must be an eternal dishonour to his memory .
divided his cavalry into three small squadrons , left all his infantry in one body , hid his arquebusiers on the road by which the inca must pass , and kept twenty of his most determined companions near himself .
, wishing to give the Spaniards a great idea of his power , advanced with the whole of his army .
He himself was borne upon a kind of bed , decorated with feathers , covered with plates of gold and silver , and ornamented with precious stones .
He was accompanied by his principal nobles , carried like himself on the shoulders of their servants , and he was surrounded by dancers and jesters .
Such a march was more that of a procession than of an army .
As soon as the inca had nearly reached the quarters ( according to ) , , the chaplain of the expedition , who was afterwards made a bishop as a reward for his conduct , advanced with the crucifix in one hand and his breviary in the other .
In an interminable discourse he set forth to the monarch the doctrine of the creation , the fall of the first man , the , , and Resurrection of our , the choice made by God of Peter to be His vicar upon earth , the power transmitted through him to the , and the gift made by to the King of of all the regions of the .
When he had expounded all these doctrines , he called upon to embrace the religion , to recognize the supreme authority of the , and to submit to the King of as his legitimate sovereign .
If he submitted immediately , undertook to promise that the king his master would take under his protection , and allow him to continue to reign there ; but he declared war against him and threatened him with fearful vengeance if he refused to obey , and persevered in his impiety .
To say the least of it , this was a singular scene and a very strange harangue , alluding to facts which were utterly unknown to the Peruvians , and of the truth of which a more skilful orator than would not have succeeded in persuading them .
If we add that the interpreter knew so little of the language that it was almost an impossibility for him to translate what he scarcely understood himself , and that the language lacked words to express ideas so foreign to its genius , we shall not be much surprised to learn that understood almost nothing of the monk 's discourse .
Some sentences , however , which attacked his own power , filled him with surprise and indignation .
But he was none the less moderate in his reply .
He said that , as master of his own kingdom by right of succession , he could not see how any one had the power to dispose of it without his consent ; he added that he was not at all willing to renounce the religion of his fathers to adopt one of which he had only heard that day for the first time ; with regard to the other points touched upon in the discourse he understood nothing , it was a thing entirely new to him , and he would much like to know where had learnt so many wonderful things .
`` In this book , '' replied , handing him his breviary .
received it with eagerness and turned over some of the leaves with much curiosity , then , putting it to his ear , he exclaimed , `` What you show me there does not speak to me , and tells me nothing . ''
With this he flung the book upon the ground .
This served as a signal for the combat , or rather for the massacre .
and muskets came into play , the cavalry sprang forward , and the infantry fell sword in hand upon the stupefied Peruvians .
In a few moments the confusion was at its height .
The fled on all sides , without attempting to defend themselves .
As to , although his principal officers tried to make a rampart of their own bodies , while they carried him off , sprang upon him , dispersed or overthrew his guards , and seizing him by his long hair , threw him down from the litter in which he was carried .
Only the darkness could arrest the carnage .
Four thousand Indians were killed , a greater number wounded , and 3000 were taken prisoners .
An incontestable proof that there was no real battle is , that of all the alone was hit , and he received his wound from one of his own soldiers who was too precipitately endeavouring to seize upon the inca .

The booty collected in the camp and from the dead exceeded anything the could have imagined , and their enthusiasm was proportioned to the conquest of such riches .

But the inca , soon understanding the unbridled covetousness of his jailors , made a proposal to Pizarro to pay him ransom , and to have a room of twenty-two feet in length by sixteen in width filled as high as the hand could reach with vases , utensils , and ornaments of gold .

In the meantime landed with 200 soldiers .
There had been set aside for him and his men -- with what regrets may easily be imagined -- 100,000 pesos ( a coin ) ; a fifth was reserved for the king , and this left 1,528,500 pesos to be divided between and his companions .
This product of pillage and massacre was solemnly divided between those entitled to it on the of , the patron saint of , after fervent prayer to God .
A deplorable mixture this of religion and profanity , too common unfortunately , in these times of mingled superstition and avarice .
Each horse-soldier received 8000 pesos as his share , and each foot-soldier 4000 , which would be equivalent to about 1600_l._ and 800_l._ sterling .
This was enough to satisfy the most exacting soldier , after a campaign which had been neither long nor difficult .
Many of the adventurers wished to enjoy this unexpected good fortune in a peaceable manner in their own country , and eagerly asked for their dismissal .
This granted without hesitation , for he felt sure that the news of their rapidly-acquired wealth would soon bring him new recruits .
With his brother , who went to to give the emperor an account of 's triumph and some splendid presents , went sixty Spaniards , laden heavily indeed with money , but lightly with remorse .
As soon as 's ransom was paid , he claimed his freedom ; but , who had only saved his life that he might make all the treasures of Peru his own , and shelter himself under the prestige and authority which the inca still exercised over his subjects , was soon wearied by his entreaties .
He suspected him also of having for some time secretly given orders to levy troops in the distant provinces of the empire .
Besides , having soon discovered that was no better educated than one of the lowest of his soldiers , felt in consequence a contempt for the governor which , unfortunately , he could not conceal .
Such were the reasons , all trivial as they were , which determined to prepare for the trial of the inca .
Nothing could have been more hateful than this trial , in which and were at the same time both suitors and judges .
The heads of the accusation were so ridiculous and absurd , that one is in doubt whether to be most surprised by the effrontery or the wickedness of , in subjecting the head of a powerful empire , over which he had no jurisdiction , to such an inquiry .
, being found guilty , was condemned to be burnt alive ; but as he had at length asked to be baptized , that he might rid himself of the importunities of , his enemies contented themselves with strangling him .
A worthy counterpart this , of 's execution !
These were amongst the most atrocious and odious deeds committed by the Spaniards in , where , however , they have sullied themselves with every imaginable crime .
Among this herd of adventurers there were still some men who had retained sentiments of honour and self-respect .
They protested loudly against this perversion of justice , but their generous pleadings were stifled by the selfish declamations of and his worthy assistants .

This road has always been one of the worst and most trying that it is possible to choose .
Before they had reached the plain of , after horrible sufferings from hunger and thirst , without speaking of the burning cinders hurled from the crater of , a volcano near , and the snow-storms which assailed them , the fifth part of the band of adventurers , and half the horses , had perished ; the remainder were completely discouraged and quite unfit for fighting .

This arrangement was made very solemnly , and they took their oath upon the consecrated wafer , that for the future they would undertake nothing against one another .

After this solemn agreement , which was destined to be observed with as little fidelity as the first , made his preparations for departure .
to his well-known liberality , as much as to his reputation for courage , he gathered together 570 men , of about equal numbers of cavalry and infantry , with which he set out by land for .
The journey was an extremely trying one , and the adventurers suffered severely from intense cold whilst crossing the ; they had also to deal with very warlike tribes , unsoftened by any civilization , who assailed them with a _furia_ of which nothing they had seen in had given them any idea .

After the new partnership had been signed between the conquerors ( 1534 ) , had returned to the provinces bordering on the sea , in which he could establish a regular government , there being no longer anything to dread from resistance .
For a man who had never studied legislation , he had drawn up some very wise rules for the administration of justice , for the collection of taxes , the apportionment of the , and the working of the mines .
Some parts of the `` conquistador 's '' character were doubtless very open to criticism , but it is only just to recognize that he was not wanting in enlarged ideas , and that he was conscientious in playing his part as the founder of a great empire .
This it was which made him hesitate long before choosing the future capital of the possessions .

Soon , the of ( de Reyes ) , or , as it is called by a corruption of the name of the river which flows at its feet , assumed the aspect of a great city , owing to the magnificent palace and the sumptuous residences for officers , which caused to be built there .
While these cares kept far from his capital , small bodies of troops , sent in different directions , penetrated into the most distant provinces of the empire , with the object of extinguishing the last smouldering embers of resistance ; so many of the soldiers were employed in this way , that there remained in itself but a very small body of troops .
The inca , who had remained in the hands of the , thought this an opportune moment for fomenting a general rising , in which he earnestly hoped that the foreign government might be overthrown .
Although closely guarded , he contrived to take his measures with so much skill that he did not arouse the suspicions of his oppressors .
He obtained permission even to be present at a grand fête , which was to be held at several miles ' distance from , and for which the most distinguished persons in the empire had met together .
As soon as the inca appeared , the standard of revolt was raised .
The country was soon in arms from the confines of the province of as far as , and a number of small detachments of Spaniards were surprised and destroyed .

The conquerors made a most valiant resistance , but experienced some severe losses , especially that of .

While this was going on , a considerable body of invested , intercepted all communications , and annihilated the various small bodies of troops which sent at intervals to the aid of the at .
At this time he sent away all his vessels to to compel his companions to make a desperate resistance ; he recalled from Truxillo the forces under the command of d'Alvarado , and entrusted to the latter a column of 500 men , which advanced to within several miles of the capital without having the slightest suspicion that the town was now in the hands of fellow-countrymen , who were fully determined to bar their passage .
But desired much rather to attract these new adversaries to himself than to destroy them ; he arranged therefore , to surprise them and make them prisoners .
He had now a fine opportunity in his hands of ending the war , and making himself master of the two governments by a single blow .
Several of his officers had observed this to him , and especially , who proposed that the two brothers of the `` conquistador '' should be put to death , and that should advance by forced marches with his victorious troops against , where , taken by surprise , would not be able to resist him .
But as a Latin poet says , `` Jupiter makes dotards of those whom he means to ruin . ''
, who in so many other instances had thrown aside all scruples , did not wish to put himself in the wrong by invading 's dominions as a rebel , and he quietly took the road back to .
Looking at it only from the side of 's own interests , he evidently committed in this a gross blunder , of which he was soon to repent ; but if we consider , what we should never lose sight of , the interest of the country , he had already committed a capital crime in the acts of aggression of which he had been guilty , and in kindling civil war in face of an enemy quite ready to take advantage of it .
His adversaries did not delay to remind him of it .
prompt decision would have been necessary for to make him master of the situation , had everything to expect from time and opportunity .
While waiting for the promised reinforcements from , he commenced negotiations with his adversary , lasting for several months , during which time one of his brothers , as well as , found means to escape with more than seventy men .
Although had been so often duped , he consented again to receive the licentiate , who was ordered to represent to him , that if the emperor knew what was taking place between the two competitors , and learnt the condition to which their contests had reduced affairs , no doubt he would recall them both , and put some one else in their place .

Scarcely had the last of his brothers been set at liberty than , rejecting all idea of peace and amicable arrangement , declared that arms alone should decide whether he or was to be lord of .
In a short time he had assembled a body of 700 men , of which he entrusted the command to his two brothers .
Finding it impossible to cross the mountains which would have been the most direct road to , they followed the line of the sea-coast as far as , and then penetrated into a branch of the Andes , by which they could reach the capital in a short time .
Possibly ought to have defended the mountain defiles , but he had only 500 men , and he reckoned much on his splendid cavalry , whom he could not deploy in a confined space ; he therefore waited for the enemy in the plain of .
The two parties encountered each other on the 26th of April , 1538 , with equal animosity ; but the victory was decided by two companies of musketeers which the emperor had sent to Pizarro when he heard of the revolt of the .
One hundred and forty soldiers perished in this engagement , which received the name of _las salinas_ .
and several officers of distinction were killed in cold blood after the battle , and himself , aged and ill , could not escape from .
The Indians who , assembled in arms on the surrounding mountains , had reckoned upon falling on the conqueror , had need instead to fly in all haste .
`` Nothing , '' says , `` more entirely proves the ascendancy gained by the over the , than seeing that the latter , witnesses of the defeat and dispersion of one of the parties , had not the courage to attack the other , even weakened and fatigued as they were by their victory , and dared not fall upon their oppressors when fortune offered them so favourable an opportunity for attacking them with advantage . ''
At this period a victory not followed by pillage was incomplete , so the town of was sacked , and all the riches that 's companions found there did not suffice to content them .
They had such exalted ideas of their merits and of the services which they had rendered , that each would have desired an appointment as governor .
therefore dispersed them , and sent them to conquer fresh territories with some of the partisans of Almagro who had rallied , and whom it was important to send to a distance .
As for himself , , feeling convinced that his name constituted a focus of permanent agitation , resolved to get rid of him .
He caused him therefore to be put upon his trial , which ended , as it was easy to foresee , in a sentence of death .
When received this news , after giving way for a few moments to a very natural grief , pleading his great age and the different way in which he had behaved with regard to and when they were his prisoners , he recovered his calmness and awaited his death with a soldier 's courage .
He was strangled in his prison , and afterwards publicly beheaded ( 1538 ) .
After several successful expeditions , set out for , to give the Emperor an account of what had taken place .
He found most minds there strangely prejudiced against him and his brothers .
Their cruelty , their violence , and their disregard of the most sacred engagements had been laid bare without reserve , by some friends of 's .
needed the utmost cleverness to win the round .
V. had no means of judging fairly on which side the justice of the case lay , for he had only heard of it from the interested parties ; he could only discern the deplorable consequences to his own government of the civil war .
He decided , therefore , to send a commissioner to the country , to whom he gave most extensive powers , and who , after having inquired into all that had taken place , should establish whatever form of government he thought most advisable .
This delicate mission was confided to , a judge of _audience_ at , who proved not unequal to his task .
One fact is worthy of notice ; he was recommended to show the greatest respect towards , at the very time when his brother was arrested and thrown into a prison , where he was destined to remain forgotten for twenty years .
While these events were taking place in , the portioned out the conquered country , keeping for himself and his trustworthy friends the most fertile and best situated districts , and giving to 's companions , the men of as they were called , only the more sterile and distant territories .
Next he confided to de , one of his aides-de-camp the execution of the project which had only been able to sketch out , the conquest of .
set out on the 28th of January , 1540 , with 150 Spaniards , amongst whom , de , and de were destined especially to distinguish themselves ; he crossed first the desert of , which even at the present day is considered a most troublesome enterprise , and reached , standing in the midst of a beautiful valley .
Received at first with great cordiality , he had to sustain , as soon as harvest was over , several combats with the Araucanians , a race of brave , indefatigable warriors , very different from the Indians of .
In spite of this , he laid the foundations of the town of on the 12th of February , 1541 .
spent eight years in , presiding over the conquest and organization of the country .
Less greedy than the other `` conquistadores '' his contemporaries , he only sought for the mineral riches of the country that he might ensure the development of the prosperity of his colony , in which he had taken care first of all to encourage agriculture .
`` The best mine that I know of , is one of corn and wine with nourishment for livestock .
Who has this , has money .
As for mines , we do not depend upon them for subsistence .
And often that which looks well outwardly is not really worth much . ''
These wise words of , in his la , might have been used by , so exactly do they correspond with and express his sentiments .
His valour , prudence , and humanity , more especially the latter quality , which shines forth strangely in contrast with the cruelty of , ensures for him a distinction all his own among the `` conquistadores '' of the sixteenth century .
[ Illustration : The shores of . ]
At the time that set out for , crossed the Andes at the head of 340 Spaniards , half of whom were mounted , and 4000 Indians , of whom the greater part of the perished from cold ; then he penetrated eastwards into the interior , seeking for a country where spices and cinnamon were said to abound .
In these vast Savannahs , intersected by marshes and virgin forests , the encountered torrents of rain , which lasted quite two months ; they found only a scattered population , who were not industrious and also hostile ; in consequence , the invaders often suffered from hunger in a country where there were then neither horses nor oxen , where the largest quadrupeds were tapirs and llamas , and even the latter were seldom met with on this slope of the Andes .
In spite of these difficulties , which would have discouraged any less energetic explorers than the _descubridores_ of the sixteenth century , they persevered in their attempt and descended the or , an affluent on the left of the , as far as its confluence .
There , with great difficulty they built a brigantine , which was manned by fifty soldiers under the command of .
But either the strength of the current carried him away , or else being no longer under the eyes of his chief , he wished in his turn to be the leader of an expedition of discovery ; he did not wait for at the appointed rendezvous , but continued to descend the river until he reached the ocean .
Such a voyage is simply marvellous , through nearly 6000 miles of an unknown region , without guide , without compass , without provisions , with a crew who murmured more than once against the foolish attempt of their leader , and in the midst of populations almost invariably hostile .
From the mouth of the river , which he had just descended in his badly built and dilapidated vessel , succeeded in reaching the , whence he set sail for .
If the proverb `` He who comes from a distance tells many lies '' were not of much earlier date , one might have thought it had been coined for .
He invented the most preposterous fables as to the wealth of the countries he had traversed ; the inhabitants were so rich that the roofs of the temples were formed of plates of gold ; an assertion which gave rise to the legend of .
had heard of the existence of a of female warriors who had founded a vast empire , which caused the river to be called the _River of the .
If , however , we strip this narrative of all that is ridiculous and grotesque , and calculated to please the imaginations of his contemporaries , it remains certain that 's expedition is one of the most remarkable of this epoch , so fertile in gigantic enterprises ; and it furnishes the first information upon the immense zone of country lying between the Andes and the .
But we must return to .
His embarrassment and consternation had been great , when on arriving at the confluence of the and , he had not found , who was to have been awaiting him .
Fearing that some accident might have befallen his lieutenant , he had descended the course of the river for 150 miles , until he met with an unfortunate officer , who had been left behind for having addressed some remonstrances to his chief upon his perfidy .
The bravest among 's men were discouraged at the news of the cowardly way in which they had been abandoned , and at the destitute condition in which they were left .
was obliged to yield to their entreaties and to return to , from which they were more than 1200 miles away .
To give an idea of their sufferings on this return journey , it suffices to say that , after having eaten horses , dogs , and reptiles , roots , and wild beasts , and after having devoured every article made of leather in their accoutrements , the unfortunate survivors who reached , lacerated by brambles , emaciated and utterly impoverished , numbered only twenty-four .
Four thousand Indians and two hundred and ten had perished in this expedition , which had lasted less than two years .
While was conducting the unfortunate expedition just related , the old partisans of , who had never frankly joined , gathered round the son of their old leader , and formed a plot for murdering the .
In vain was several times warned of what was threatening him , he would pay no heed to the report .
He said `` Keep quiet , I shall be safe as long as there is no one in Peru who does not know that I can in a moment take the life of any one who should dare to form the project of attempting mine . ''
On Sunday , the 26th of June , 1541 , at the hour of siesta , de and eighteen conspirators left the house of 's son with drawn swords in their hands and armed from top to toe .
They ran towards the house of , crying out , `` Death to the tyrant !
death to the infamous wretch ! ''
They entered the palace , killed de , who had appeared in haste on hearing the noise , and gained the hall , where was , with his brother Francisco-Martin , the doctor , and a dozen servants .
These jumped out of the windows , with the exception of , two other gentlemen , and two tall pages , who were killed while defending the door of the governor 's apartment .
He himself had not had time to put on his cuirass , but he seized his sword and buckler and defended himself valiantly , killing four of his adversaries and wounding several others .
One of his assailants , in a spirit of self-devotion , attracted to himself the blows of .
Meanwhile the other conspirators made their way in and attacked him with such fury that he could not parry all the blows , being so exhausted that he could scarcely wield his sword .
`` Thus , '' says , `` they made an end , and succeeded in killing him by a thrust in the throat .
Falling to the ground , he asked in a loud voice that he might be allowed to confess , and then not being able any longer to speak , he made the sign of the cross on the ground , which he kissed , and then yielded up his soul to God . ''
Some negroes carried his body to the church , where , his old servant , alone ventured to come and claim it .
This faithful servant secretly rendered to it funeral honours , for the conspirators had pillaged the house of , not leaving enough even to pay for wax tapers .
Thus did come to his end , assassinated even in the capital of the vast empire which owed to his valour and indefatigable perseverance , but which he bestowed upon his country , it must be admitted , ravaged , decimated , and drowned in a deluge of blood .
is often compared with ; the one had as much ambition , courage , and military capacity as the other ; but the cruelty and avarice of the della were carried to an extreme in , and united in him to perfidy and duplicity .
If we are inclined to excuse certain parts of ' character which are not estimable , by the times in which he lived , we are at least charmed by that grace and nobility of manners , and by that way of a gentleman above prejudices , which made him so much beloved by the soldier .
In , on the contrary , we find roughness , and a harsh , unsympathizing way of feeling , while his chivalrous qualities disappear entirely behind the rapacity and perfidy which are the salient features of his character .
If found brave and resolute adversaries among the , who opposed almost insurmountable difficulties to his progress , had no trouble in vanquishing the Peruvians , who were timid and enervated , and who never made any serious resistance to his arms .
Of the conquests of and , the less difficult produced the greater metallurgic advantage to , and thus it was the more appreciated .
The civil war was on the point of breaking out again after 's death when the governor arrived , who was delegated by the metropolitan government .
As soon as he had collected the needful troops , he marched towards .
He seized young Almagro without trouble , had him beheaded with forty of his confederates and governed the country with firmness , until the viceroy , arrived .
It is not our intention to enter into the detail of the disputes which took place between the latter and , who , profiting by the general discontent , caused by the new regulations as to the `` repartimientos , '' revolted against the 's representative .
After many changes of fortune , for which we have not space , the struggle ended by the defeat and execution of , which took place in 1548 .
His body was taken to and buried fully dressed ; `` No one , '' says la Vega , `` being willing to give even a winding-sheet for it . ''
Thus ended the judicial assassin of .

He had been brought up in the house of King , where he received as complete an education as could then be given him .
After having made mathematics and navigation his special study -- for at this time in there was an irresistible current which drew the whole country towards maritime expeditions and discoveries -- early embraced a maritime career , and embarked in 1505 with , who was on his way to the .
He took part in the sacking of , and in all the events of that campaign .

On his return to , obtained leave , though not without difficulty , to search through the royal archives .
He soon became certain that the were situated in the hemisphere which the bull of demarcation adopted at by the kings of and , and confirmed in 1494 by VI. , had given to .
In virtue of this line of demarcation , which was destined to give rise to so many impassioned debates , all the countries situated at 360 miles west of the meridian of the de were to belong to , and all those lying to the east of the same meridian to .
was of too active a nature to remain long without again taking service ; he went next to fight in at , a town in , where he received a slight wound in his knee , but one which by injuring a nerve made him lame for the remainder of his life , and obliged him to return to .
Conscious of the superiority which his theoretical and practical knowledge and his services had earned for him above the herd of courtiers , naturally felt more keenly than another would have done the unjust treatment he received from with regard to certain complaints laid by the people of against the officers .
King 's prejudices soon changed to a real dislike .
It showed itself by the outrageous imputation that was pretending to suffer from a wound which was really of no consequence and was completely cured , that he might escape from accusations which he could not refute .
Such an assertion was a serious matter for the honour of , so susceptible and suspicious ; he thereupon came to a desperate determination which corresponded moreover with the greatness of the insult which he had received .
That no one might be ignorant of it , he caused it to be legally set forth that he renounced his rights as a citizen , and changed his nationality , and he then took out letters of naturalization in .
This was to proclaim , as solemnly as could possibly be done , that he intended to be looked upon as a subject of the crown of , to which henceforward he would consecrate his services and his whole life .
This was a serious determination , as we can see , which no one blamed , and which even the most severe historians , such as and y Sousa , have excused .
At the same time as , the licentiate left with his brother and a merchant named de ; the former was a man deeply versed in cosmographical knowledge , and had equally with fallen under 's displeasure .
had entered into a treaty of partnership with to reach the Moluccas by a new way , but one which was not otherwise specified , and which remained 's secret .
As soon as they arrived in , ( 1517 ) , the two partners submitted their project to , who accepted it in principle ; but there remained the always delicate question touching the means for putting it into execution .
Happily , found in de , the factor of the Chamber of , an enthusiastic partisan of his theories , and one who promised to exert all his influence to make the enterprise a success .
He had an interview accordingly with the high Chancellor , the and of , .
He set forth with such skill the great advantage that would derive from the discovery of a route leading to the very centre of the spice production , and the great prejudice which it would cause to the trade of , that an agreement was signed on the 22nd of March , 1518 .
The undertook to pay all the expenses of the expedition on condition that the greater part of the profits should belong to him .
But had still many obstacles to surmount before taking to the sea .
In the first place there were the remonstrances of the ambassador , de , who , seeing that his endeavours were in vain , even tried to compass the assassination of , so says y Sousa .
Then he encountered the ill-will of the employés of the de contratacion_ at , who were jealous of a stranger being entrusted with the command of such an important expedition , and envious of the least token of favour which had been accorded to and , who had been named commanders of the order of .
But had given his consent by a public act , which seemed to be irrevocable .
They tried , however , to make the Emperor alter his decision by organizing , on the 22nd of October , 1518 , a disturbance paid for with gold .
It broke out on the pretext that , who had just had one of his ships drawn on shore for repairs and painting , had decorated it with the arms .
This last attempt failed miserably , and three statutes of the 30th of March , and 6th and 30th of April , fixed the composition of the crews and named the staff ; while a final official document dated from the 26th of July , 1519 , confided the sole command of the expedition to .
What had meanwhile been happening to ?
But this man , who had up to this time been treated on the same footing as , and who had perhaps first conceived the project , now found himself quite excluded from the command of the expedition , after some dissensions of which the cause is unknown .
His health , already shaken , received a last shock from this affront , and poor Rey Faleiro , who had become almost childish , having returned to to see his family , was arrested there , and only released upon the intercession of At last , after having sworn fidelity and homage to the crown of , received in his turn the oath of his officers and sailors , and left the port of de on the morning of the 10th of , 1519 .
But before entering on the narrative of this memorable campaign , we must give a few particulars of the man who has left us the most complete account of it , or as he is often called in .
Born at about 1491 , of a noble family , formed part of the suite of the , sent by X. to , who was then at .
His attention was no doubt aroused by the noise which the preparations for the expedition made at that time in , and he obtained permission to take part in the voyage .
This volunteer proved an excellent recruit , for he showed himself in every respect as faithful and intelligent an observer as he was a brave and courageous companion .
He was wounded at the battle of , fighting beside , which prevented him from being present at the banquet during which so many of his companions were destined to lose their lives .
As to his narrative , with the exception of some exaggerations of detail according to the taste of that time , it is exact , and the greater part of the descriptions which we owe to him have been verified by modern travellers and learned men , especially by M. Alcide d'Orbigny .
Upon his return to on the 6th of September , 1522 , after having fulfilled the vow which he had made to go bare-foot to return thanks to _Nuesta de la Victoria_ , the ( as they called him on board the , ) presented to , then at , a complete journal of the voyage .
When he returned to , by means of the original as well as of some supplementary notes , he wrote a longer narrative of the expedition , at the request of .

He sent copies of this work to several distinguished personages , and notably to of , mother of I .

Some critics , however , suppose that this narrative must have been written originally in ; they found their opinion upon the existence of three manuscripts of the sixteenth century , which give very different readings , and of which two are deposited in the at .
